## 1.1 +1.2+1.3 Introduction to Physics + Physical Ouantities + International System of Units

1. Define atomic physics and nuclear physics.
   (FSD. GII, RWP. GII, 2015)
   (GRW. GI, RWP. GII, 2016) (LHR. GI, BWP. GII, 2017) (FSD. GI \& GII, SWL GII, 2019) (SWL GI, SGD. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Atomic Physics: It is the study of the structure and properties of atoms.
   Nuclear physics: It deals with the properties and behaviour of nuclei and the particles within the nuclei.
2. Define Mechanics and Geophysics.
   (MLN. GII, 2015) (DGK. GI, 2016) (DGK. GII, 2017)
   Ans. Mechanics: This branch of physics is the study of motion of objects, its causes and effect.
   Geophysics: It is the study of the internal structure of the Earth.
3. Differentiate between Plasma Physics and Geo Physics. (SGD. GI, BWP. GII, 2014) (GRW. GI, 2015) (RWP. GI, 2016)
   (GRW. GI, 2017) (LHR. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2018) (SGD. GI, RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, SWL, GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)
   Ans. Plasma Physics: It is the study of production, properties of the ionic state of matter-the fourth state of matter.
4. Define physical sciences and biological sciences.
   (LMR. GII, 2019)
   Ans. Physical sciences: Physical sciences which deals with the study of non-living things.
   Biological sciences: Biological sciences which are concerned with the study of living things.
5. Write down the SI units of temperature, electric current, force and electric charge.(urr.G. 2022)

Ans.

|    Quantities    |  Unit   |
| :--------------: | :-----: |
|   Temperature    | Kelvin  |
| Electric current | A'mpere |
|      Force       | Newton  |
| Electric charge  | Coulomb |

6. Define mechanics and heat.
   (DGK. GII. 2022)
   Ans. Mechanics: This branch of physics is the study of motion of objects, its causes and effect.
   Heat: This branch of physics deals with the nature of heat, modes of transfer and effects of heat.
7. Differentiate between sound and light.

Ans. Sound: It deals with the physical aspects of sound waves, their production, properties and applications.
Light: It is the study of physical aspects of sound waves, their production, properties and applications. 8. Which base quantities has units mole and Kelvin?
(RWP. GII, 2017)
Ans. Mole: Amount of substance
Kelvin: Temperature 9. Write SI units and symbols of the following quantities:
(SWL GI, 2018) (DGK GII, 2021) length, mass, temperature, electric current.
Ans.

|       Name       | Symbol |          SI unit           |
| :--------------: | :----: | :------------------------: |
|      Length      | $\ell$ |    metre $(\mathrm{m})$    |
|       Mass       |   m    | kilogramme $(\mathrm{kg})$ |
|   Temperature    |   T    |   kelvin $(\mathrm{K})$    |
| Electric Current |   I    |   Ampere $(\mathrm{A})$    |

10. Write the names of two derived quantities and their SI units.
    (RWP. GII, 2019)
    Ans.

| Derived quantities |                  SI Unit                   |
| :----------------: | :----------------------------------------: |
|       Speed        |             $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}$             |
|      Pressure      | $\mathrm{Pa}\left(\mathrm{Nm}^{-2}\right)$ |

11. Differentiate base units and derived units. (DGK. GI, 2015) (SGD. GI, GRW. GI, BWP. GI, 2016)
    (FSD. GI \& GII, SWL GII, SGD. GI \& GII, RWP. GII, BWP. GI, 2018) (GRW. GII, SWL GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, SGD. GII, 2021) (LHR. GI, 2022) (SGD. GI, 2023)
    Ans.

| Base units                                                                                                                                           | Derived units                                                                  |
| :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The units that describe base quantities <br> are called base units. <br> Each base quantity has its SI units. <br> e.g. second, meter, kilogram etc. | The units used to measure derived quantities are <br> called derived units. OR |
| Derived units are defined in terms of base units and                                                                                                 |                                                                                |
| are obtained by multiplying or dividing one or more                                                                                                  |                                                                                |
| base units with each other.                                                                                                                          |                                                                                |
| e.g. Newton, Pascal, Coulomb etc.                                                                                                                    |                                                                                |

12. Write the names of four derived units,

Ans. Spetd, acceleration, volume, foree 13. What is meant by derived quantitites and derived units?

$$
\mathrm{mS}^{\top}, \mathrm{ms}^{-2}, \mathrm{~m}^{3}, \text { (DGK GII, 2015)(BWP. GII, 2021) }
$$

(GRW. Gl, 2022)
Ans. Derived quantitites: The quantities that are expressed in terms of base quantities are called derived quantities.
Examples: Volume, speed, force

Derived Units: The units used to measure derived quantities are called derived units.
Examples:

1. Unit of speed is $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}$.
2. Unit of volume is $\mathbf{m}^{3}$.
3. Pick out the base unit in the following: Watt, Newton, Metre, Ampere, Mole
   (MLN. GII, 2023)
   Ans. Base unit: Mole, Ampere, metre.

## 1.4 + 1.5 Prefixes + Scientific Notation

1. Estimate the age of 16 years in seconds.
   (GRW. GI, 2023)
   Ans. (year) $1=325$ (days)
   (year) $1=365 \times 24$ (Hours)
   (year) $1=8760$ (Hours)
   (year) $1=8760 \times 60$ (minutes)
   (year) $1=525600$ (minutes)
   (year) $1=525600 \times 60(\mathrm{sec})$
   (year) $1=31536000(\mathrm{sec})$
   (years) $16=16 \times 31536000(\mathrm{sec})$
   (years) $16=504576000(\mathrm{sec})$
2. Express the following quantities using prefixes. (a) $\mathbf{5 0 0 0 g}$ (b) $\mathbf{5 2} \times \mathbf{1 0}^{\mathbf{- 1 0}} \mathbf{g}$ (MLN. Gl, SWL Gl, 2018)

Ans. (a) $5000 \mathrm{~g}=5 \times 1000 \mathrm{~g}$

$$
\begin{aligned}
& =5 \times 1 \mathrm{~kg} \\
5000 \mathrm{~g} & =5 \mathrm{~kg}
\end{aligned}
$$

3. Convert 12 years into seconds.
   (SWL GII, 2022)

$$
\begin{aligned}
& \text { Sol.Age }=12 \text { years } \\
& 1 \text { year }=12 \text { months } \\
& 1 \text { year }=365 \text { days } \\
& 1 \text { year }=365 \times 24 \text { hours }=8760 \text { hours } \\
& 1 \text { year }=8760 \times 60 \mathrm{~min}=525600 \mathrm{~min} \\
& 1 \text { year }=525600 \times 60 \mathrm{sec}=31536000 \mathrm{sec} \\
& 12 \text { years }=12 \times 31536000 \mathrm{sec} \\
& 12 \text { years }=378432000 \mathrm{sec}
\end{aligned}
$$

(b) $52 \times 10^{-10} \mathrm{~g}=5.2 \times 10^{1} \times 10^{-10} \mathrm{~g}$

$$
\begin{aligned}
& =5.2 \times 10^{1-10} \mathrm{~g} \\
& =5.2 \times 10^{-9} \mathrm{~g} \because 10^{-9} \mathrm{~g}=1 \mathrm{ng} \\
& =5.2 \mathrm{ng}
\end{aligned}
$$

4. Your hair grow at the rate of 1 mm per day. Find their growth rate in $\mathrm{nm} \mathrm{s}^{-1}$.
   (DGK. GII, 2022)
   Ans. Given Data: growth rate $=1 \mathrm{~mm} /$ day
   growth rate $=1 \times 10^{-3} \mathrm{~m} /$ day
   Required: growth rate in $\mathrm{nms}^{-1}=$ ?
   Calculations: First we convert days into seconds
   As; 1 day = 24 hours
   1 hour $\quad=60$ minutes
   1 minute $=60$ seconds
   So; 1 day $\quad=24 \times 60 \times 60$ seconds
   1 day $\quad=86400 \mathrm{~s}$
   Now we convert " m " in " nm "
   As;

$$
\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{1 \times 10^{-3} \mathrm{~m}}{10^{-9}} \times 10^{-9} \\
& =1 \times 10^{-3} \times 10^{+9} \times 10^{-9} \mathrm{~m} \\
& =10^{+6} \mathrm{~nm} \\
& {\left[\because 10^{-9} \mathrm{~m}=1 \mathrm{~nm}\right]}
\end{aligned}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\text { growthrate }=\frac{10^{6} \mathrm{~nm}}{86400}
$$

growth rate in $\mathrm{nms}^{-1}=11.57 \mathrm{nms}^{-1}$ 5. Write the numbers given below in scientific notation.
(a) 0.0000000016 g (b) 6400000 m

Ans. (a) $0.0000000016 \mathrm{~g}=0.0000000016=1.6 \times 10^{-9} \mathrm{~g}$
(b) $6400000 \mathrm{~m} \quad=6400000=6.4 \times 10^{6} \mathrm{~m}$ 6. Define Physical quantities and Scientific notation.

Ans. Physical quantities: All measurable quantities are physical quantities.
Examples: Length, Mass, Time.
Scientific notation: It is a way to express a given number as a number between 1 and 10 multiplied by 10 having an appropriate power.
Example: The moon is 384000000 metres away from the Earth. Distance of the Moon from the Earth can also be expressed as $3.84 \times 10^{8} \mathrm{~m}$. 7. How many seconds in one year? Write in Scientific notation.
(DGK GII, 2021)
Ans.

|    Number of days in one year | $=365$ days                            |
| ----------------------------: | :------------------------------------- |
|   Number of hours in one year | $=365 \times 24=8760$ hours            |
| Number of minutes in one year | $=8760 \times 60=525600 \mathrm{~min}$ |
| Number of seconds in one year | $=525600 \times 60 \mathrm{sec}$       |
|                               | $=31536000 \mathrm{sec}$               |
|                               | $=3.1536 \times 10^{7} \mathrm{sec}$   |

8. Express these numbers in scientific notation.
   (a) 0.0000548 s
   (b) 6400000 m
   (FSD. GL, 2022)
   Ans.
   (a) $0.0000548 \mathrm{~s}=5.48 \times 10^{-5} \mathrm{~s}$
   (b) $6400000 \mathrm{~m}=6.4 \times 10^{6} \mathrm{~m}$
9. Write estimate one day in seconds.
   (MLN. GII, 2023)
   Ans. Seconds in a day

## As we know

1 day $=24$ hours
1 hour $=60$ minutes
1 minute $=60$ seconds
So
1 day $=24 \times 60 \times 60$ seconds
1 day $=86400 \mathrm{~s}$
1 day $=86400 \mathrm{~s}$
Multiplying \& dividing by $10^{4}$

$$
\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{86400}{10000} \times 10^{4} \mathrm{~s} \\
& =8.64 \times 10^{4} \mathrm{~s}
\end{aligned}
$$

### 1.6 Measuring Instruments

1. What is meant by significant figures of a measurement?
   (MLM, GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2017)
   Ans. All the accurately known digits and the first doubtful digit in an expression are called significant figures. Significant figure reflects the precision of a measured value of a physical quantity.
2. Write the name of two measuring instruments.
   (LHR. GII, 2017) (MLM. GI, 2022)
   Ans. Metre rule, measuring tape.
3. Define least count. What is the least count of a meter rod?
   (RWP. GI, BWP. GII, 2014) (GRW. GI, 2015) (SGD. GII, 2016) (FSD. GI, 2017) (RWP. GII, 2018) (SGD. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GII, DGK. GII, 2019)
   Ans. Least count: The smallest reading that can be measured from any instrument is called least count. The least count of metre rod is 1 mm .
4. Differentiate between electronic balance and physical balance. (BWP.GI, 2016)(DGK GI, 2018)(RWP. GII, 2022)

Ans. Electronic balance: Electronic balances come in various ranges, milligram, gram ranges and kilogramme ranges. Before measuring the mass of a body, it is switched on and its reading is set to zero. Next place the object to be weighed. The reading on the balance gives you the mass of the body placed over it.
Physical balance: A Physical balance is used in the laboratory to measure the mass of various objects by comparison. It consists of a beam resting at the centre on a fulcrum. The beam carries scale pans over the hooks on either side. 5. Differentiate between Mechanical Stopwatch and Digital Stopwatch. (BWP. GL, 2014)(SWL, GII, 2018)

Ans. Mechanical stopwatch: A machinal stopwatch can measure a time interval up to minimum 0.1 second.
Digital stopwatch: Digital stopwatch is commonly used in laboratories can measure a time interval as small as $1 / 100$ second or 0.01 second. 6. Write the procedure to measure the volume of an irregular shaped solid.
(RWP. GII, 2014) (SGD. GII, DGK GII, 2016) (BWP. GL. 2018)
Ans. Measuring volume of an irregular shaped solid: Measuring cylinder can be used to find the volume of a small irregular shaped solid that sinks in water.
Volume of a small stone can be found out as following:

1. Take some water in a graduated measuring cylinder.
2. Note the volume $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{i}}$ of water in the cylinder. 3. Tie the solid with a thread.
3. Lower the solid into the cylinder till it is fully immersed in water.
4. Note the volume $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{f}}$ of water and the solid. 6. Volume of the solid will be $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{f}}-\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{i}}$.
5. When the zero error of screw gauge will be positive?
   (GRW. GII, 2017)
   Ans. Zero error will be positive if zero of circular scale is behind the index line.
6. Write down the formula to calculate the least count of screw gauge.
   (SWL GII, RWP, GII, 2017)
   Ans. Least count of a screw gauge is 0.01 mm or 0.001 cm . It can be found by given below;
   Least Count =

$$
\frac{\text { Pitch of the screw gauge }}{\text { no. of divisions on circular scale }}
$$

9. What is digital stop watch? Tell its least count.
   (SGD. GII, 2017) (DGK GII. 2019)
   (SGD. GII, 2017) (DGK GII. 2019)
   Ans. Digital stopwatch is commonly used in laboratories can measure a time interval as small as $1 / 100$ second or 0.01 second.
   Least count: The least count for digital stop watch is 0.01 second.
10. Why use of zero error is essential in measuring instruments?

Ans. Zero error is necessary in measuring instrument to obtain an extreme correct value. 11. When the zero error of screw guage will be negative?
(RWP. Gl, 2018) (SGD. Gl, 2019)
Ans. Zero error of screw guage will be negative if zero of circular scale has crossed the index line. 12. Write two important parts of vernier callipers.
(DGK. GI, 2018) (SGD. GI, 2021)
Ans. Main scale, Vernier scale 13. What is stop watch? Write the least count of mechanical stop watch.
(GRW. GI, 2019)
Ans. A stop watch is used to measure the time internal of an event.
Least count of mechanical stop watch is 0.1 sec . 14. What is vernier callipers? Write the Least Count (L.C) of vernier callipers.
(MLN. GII, 2018) (GRW. GII, SWL. GII, BWP. GI, 2019) (SWL. GI, 2021)
Ans. Vernier caliper is an instrument which is used to measure small lengths such as internal or external diameter or length of a cylinder, etc.
The least count of vernier callipers is 0.1 mm or 0.01 cm . 15. Define Zero Error and Zero Correction.
(MLN. GI \& GII, 2019)
Ans. Zero error: If the zero of the main scale does not coincide with the zero of the vernier scale, when the jaws closed there is zero error in the instrument.
Zero correction: To remove the error in the instrument is called zero correction. 16. Why "Screw Gauge" is considered more-useful than "Vernier Calliper"?
(MLM. GI, 2019)
Ans. The instrument, screw gauge is more precise than vernier callipers because the least count of vernier calliper is 0.01 cm while the least count of screw gauge is 0.001 cm . 17. How least count of vernier callipers can be calculated?
(GRW. GI, 2021) (RWP. GI, 2022)
Ans. Least count of vernier callipers can be calculated by the following formula.

$$
\text { Least count }=\frac{\text { Smallest reading on main scale }}{\text { Number of divisions on vernier scale }}
$$

$=\frac{1 \mathrm{~mm}}{10}=0.1 \mathrm{~mm}=0.01 \mathrm{~cm}$ 18. Write down two demerits of measuring instruments used in the past.
(GRW. GII, 2022)
Ans. 1. Measuring instruments used in the past were not so reliable and accurate as we use today. For example, sun dial, water clock and other time measuring devices used around 1300 AD were quite crude. On the other hand, digital clocks and watches used now-a-days are highly reliable and accurate. 2. Pots were used to measure grain in various parts of the world in the ancient times. However, balances were also in use by Greeks and Romans. 19. Write any two factors on which accuracy in measuring a physical quantity depends.
(FSD.GII, 2022)
Ans. The accuracy in measuring a physical quantity depends upon the following factors:
A The quantity of the measuring instrument. The skill of the observer.
4 The number of the observation made. 20. What is meant by positive and negative zero error of screw gauge?
(SWL GII, 2022) (MLN. GI, 2023)
Ans. Positive zero error: Zero error will be positive if zero of circular scale is behind the index line.
Negative zero error: Zero error will be negative if zero of circular scale has crossed the index line. 21. A screw gauge has 50 divisions on its circular scale. The pitch of screw gauge is 0.5 mm . What is its least count?
(SGD. GI, 2022)
Ans. Data: Divisions on the circular scale of screw gauge $=50$ division
Pitch of the screw gauge $=0.5 \mathrm{~mm}$
Required: Least count of the screw gauge = ?

## Formula:

$$
\begin{aligned}
\text { Least count } & =\frac{\text { Pitch }}{\text { Number of divisions on circular scale }} \\
\text { Least count } & =\frac{0.5 \mathrm{~mm}}{50 \text { divisions }} \\
\text { Least count } & =0.01 \mathrm{~mm} \\
\text { Least count } & =0.01 \mathrm{~mm}=0.001 \mathrm{~cm}
\end{aligned}
$$

22. What is vernier callipers? Write down the least count of digital vernier callipers.
    (GRW. GII, 2023)
    Ans. Vernier caliper is an instrument which is used to measure small lengths such as internal or external diameter or length of a cylinder, etc.
    The least count of digital vernier callipers is 0.01 mm .
23. Why Digital Electronic Balance is more accurate than Beam Balance?

Ans. A sensitive beam balance may be able to detect a change as small as of 0.1 g or 100 mg . Where some digital balances measure even smaller difference of a the order of 0.001 g or 0.1 mg . That is the reason, digital electronic balances is more accurate then beam balances.

### 1.7 Significant Figures

1. What is meant by significant figures? How many significant figures are in 0.027 ?
   (RWP. GI, SWL. GII, 2015) (SWL. GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2016) (BWP. GI, 2018) (GRW. GI, SWL GI, 2019) (SGD. GI, 2022) (MLN. GI, DGK, GI, 2023)
   Ans. All the accurately known digits and the first doubtful digit in an expression are called significant figures. It reflects the precision of a measured value of a physical quantity.
   In 0.027, there are 2 significant figures.
2. Find the number of singnificant figures in 0.00580 km . Also express it in scientific notation.

Ans. Number of significant figures is 3 .
(RWP. Gl, 2017)

$$
0.00580 \mathrm{~km}=5.80 \times 10^{-3} \mathrm{~km}
$$

3. Write the number of significance figures in each case:
   (LHR GI, 2022)
   (i) 275.00
   (ii) 0.027

Ans. i. 275.00 has 5 significant digits. ii. 0.027 has 2 significant digits. 4. Write down rules to find the significant figures in measurement.
(BWP. GII, 2017) (BWP. GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (SGD. GII, 2022) (LHR. GI, GRW. GI, RWP. GI, 2023)
Ans. Rules to identify the significant figures.
The following rules are helpful to identifying significant figure.

1. Non-zero digits are always significant.
2. Zeros between two significant figures are also significant.
3. Final or ending zeros on the right in decimal fraction are significant.
4. Zeros written on left side of the decimal point for the purpose of spacing the decimal point are not significant.
5. In whole numbers that end in one or more zeros without a decimal point. These zeros may or may not be significant.

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

1.2: What is the difference between base quantities and derived quantities? Give three examples in each case. (GRW. GI, DGK. GI, 2014) (GRW. GII, FSD. GII, RWP. GII, 2015) (LHR. GII, MLN. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2016)

Ans.
(LHR. GII, DGK. GII, BWP. GI, 2017) (FSD. GI \& GII, DGK. GI, BWP. GII, RWP. GI, 2021) (RWP. GI, BWP, GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI, 2023)

| Base Quantities                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Derived Quantities                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ⇒ Base quantities are the quantities on the basis of which other quantities are expressed. <br> ⇒ Length, mass, time, electric current, temperature, intensity of light and amount of substance are examples of base quantities. | ⇒ The quantities that are expressed in terms of base quantities are called derived quantities. <br> ⇒ Volume, speed, force, work, energy, power and electric charge are some examples of derived quantities. |

1.3: Pick out the base units in the following:
joule, newton, kilogramme, hertz, mole, ampere, metre, kelvin, coulomb and watt
Ans. kilogramme, mole, ampere, metre and kelvin are the base units.
1.4. Find the base quantities involved in each of the following derived quantities.
(a) speed
(b) volume
(c) force
(d) work
(a) Speed:

Ans. The formula of speed is:

$$
\begin{gathered}
\text { Speed }=\frac{\text { distance covered by body }}{\text { time taken }} \\
\text { Unit of Speed }=\frac{\text { metre }}{\text { second }}=\mathrm{ms}^{-1}
\end{gathered}
$$

⇒ Unit of speed shows that speed is a derived quantity and it is derived from length and time. Metre is the unit of length and second is the unit of time.
⇒ . Length and time are base quantities.
(b) Volume:

Ans. The formula of volume is:
Volume $=$ Length × width × height
Unit of volume:Volume $=$ metre × metre × metre $=\mathrm{m}^{3}$
⇒ The unit of volume shows that volume is a derived quantity and is obtained from the length.
⇒ Length is a base quantity and its unit is metre.
(d) Work:

Ans. The formula of work is:
Work $=\mathrm{F} \times \mathrm{S}$
Unit of work:
work $=\mathrm{kgms}^{-2} \times \mathrm{m}=\mathrm{kgm}^{2} \mathrm{~s}^{-2}$
⇒ Unit of work shows that it is a derived quantity.
Work is derived from the mass, length and time.
⇒ Mass, length and time are base quantities.
(c) Force:

Ans. The formula of force is:
Force $=$ mass × acceleration
$\mathrm{F}=\mathrm{m} \times \mathrm{a}$
Unit of force:Force $=$ kilogramme × metre
per second per second
$=\mathrm{kg} \mathrm{ms}^{-2}$
⇒ The unit of mass is kilogramme, the unit of length is metre and the unit of time is second.
⇒ The unit of force shows that it is a derived quantity.
⇒ Force is derived from mass, length and time. Mass, length and time are base quantities
I.5: Estimate your age in seconds.

Ans. Supposed age of a person
Total days in one year
Total days in 15 years
Total hours in one day
Total hours in 5475 days
Total minutes in one hours
Total minutes in 131,400 hours
Total seconds in one minutes
Total seconds in 7884000 minutes
15 years of age
By the given method you can convert your exact age into seconds.
1.6: What role SI units have played in the development of science?

Ans. SI units have played a very important role in the development of science.
SI units are very helpful to exchange scientific and technical information at the international level.
1.7: What is meant by vernier constant?(LHR.GII,FSD.GI,MLN.GII,2021)(RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2022) (MLN. GII, SWL.GI, BWP. GI, 2023)

Ans. The least count of the vernier callipers is also called the vernier constant. It can be defined as:
The difference between one small division on main scale division and one vernier scale division is 0.1 mm . It is called least count (LC) of the vernier callipers.
Least count of the vernier callipers can also be found as given below.

$$
\text { Least count of vernier callipers }=\frac{\text { Smallest reading on the main scale }}{\text { Number of divisions on vernier scale }}
$$

(LHR. G. FSD. GI. DGK. GI, 2014) (FSD. GII, 2016) (LHR. GI, FSD. GI, 2017) (SWL. GI, RWP. GI, 2022)

$$
\begin{aligned}
& =15 \text { years. } \\
& =365 \text { days. } \\
& =365 \times 15=5475 \text { days } \\
& =24 \text { hours. } \\
& =5475 \times 24=131,400 \text { hours } \\
& =60 \text { minutes } \\
& =131,400 \times 60=7884000 \text { minutes } \\
& =60 \text { seconds. } \\
& =7884000 \times 60 \\
& =473,040,000 \text { seconds }
\end{aligned}
$$

(LHR. GI. 2016) (GRW. GII. 2022)

### 2.4 Terms Associated with Motion

1. Unit of velocity is:
   (GRW. GII, SWL. GI, RWP. GII, 2016) (RWP. GI, 2019)
   (A) m
   (B) $\mathrm{msec}^{-2}$
   (C) $\mathrm{msec}^{-1}$
   (D) $\mathrm{m}^{3}$

   (LHR GI, 2017)
   (A) $5 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
   (B) $10 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
   (C) $15 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
   (D) $20 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
3. A sprinter completes its 100 metre race in 12 s , its average speed will be:
   (RWP. Gl, 2017)
   (A) $100 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
   (B) $12 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
   (C) $8 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
   (D) $8.33 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$

   (RWP. GII, 2019)
   (A) Linear motion
   (B) Vibratory motion
   (C) Rotatory motion
   (D) Random motion

   (DGK. Gl, 2019)

   (B) $\pi r$
   (C) $\frac{\pi r}{2}$
   (D) $\frac{2}{3} \pi r$

   (DGK. GII, 2022)
   (A) Speed
   (B) Velocity
   (C) Acceleration
   (D) Deceleration

Answers 1. $\mathrm{msec}^{-1} 2.15 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1} 3.8 .33 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ 4. Vibratory motion 5. $\pi \mathrm{r}$ 6. $\frac{10}{36} \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ 7. Velocity

xii. A car starts from rest. It acquires a speed of $25 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ after 20 s . The distance moved by the car during this time is:
(SGD. GII, 2014) (SGD. GII, 2017)
(a) 31.25 m
(b) 250 m
(c) 500 m
(d) 5000 m

Answers
i. Line without rotation
iv. parallel to time-axis
ii. rotatory motion
v. at rest
iii. displacement
viii. velocity
xii. 250 m
vi. distance travelled by the car is 75 m vii.

ix. zero

## 2.2+2.3 Types of Motion + Scalars and Vectors

1. Define Translatory motion and give an example. (DGK. GI, 2015) (FSD. GI, 2017) (LHR. GI, SGD. GI, 2018) (BWP. GI, 2019)

Ans. Translatory motion: Translatory motion is a type of motion in which a body moves along a line without any rotation. This line may be straight or curved.
Example: A car moving in a straight line has translational motion. 2. Define Translatory Motion and Linear Motion.
(FSD. GI \& GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GII, 2016) (GRW. GII, 2023)
Ans. Translatory motion: Translatory motion is a type of motion in which a body moves along a line without any rotation. This line may be straight or curved.
Linear motion: Straight line motion of a body is known as its linear motion. 3. Differentiate between Random and Linear motion.
(SWL GI \& GII, 2019) (BWP. GII, 2023)
Ans. Difference between Random and Linear motion:

| Random motion                                                                                                                                                         | Linear motion                                                                                                                                                                     |
| :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 1. The disordered or irregular motion of an object is called random motion. <br> 2. The motion of dust or smoke particles in the air is the example of random motion. | 1. Straight line motion of a body is known as its linear motion. <br> 2. Aeroplanes flying straight in air and objects falling vertically down are the examples of linear motion. |

4. Differentiate between the circular motion and rotatory motion. (GRW. GI, RWP. GI, 2019)(LHR. GII, 2022)
   Ans. Difference between the circular motion and rotatory motion:
   | Circular Motion | Rotatory Motion |
   | :--- | :--- |
   | 1. The motion of an object in a circular path is known as circular motion. <br> 2. | 2. The motion of the Earth about its own axis is rotatory motion. |

5. Define Translatory Motion and Rotatory Motion.

Ans. Translatory motion: In translator motion, a body moves along a line without any rotation. The line may be straight or curves.
Rotatory motion: The spinning motion of a body about its axis is called rotatory motion.

### 2.4 Terms Associated with Motion

1. Convert $50 \mathrm{kmh}^{-1}$ speed of a body into $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}$.(GRW. GI, SWL GI, 2016)(BWP. GII, 2017)(LHR. GI, 2021)(RWP. GI \& GI, 2022)

Sol. Speed in $\mathrm{kmh}^{-1}=50 \mathrm{kmh}^{-1}$
Speed in $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}=\frac{50 \times 1000}{3600} \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
Speed in $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}=13.89 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ 2. Define gravitational acceleration and write its value.
(GRW. GII, FSD. GI, 2014)
(FSD. GII, RWP. GII, 2015) (SWL. GII, RWP. GII, MLN. GI, 2016) (RWP. GII, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2017) (FSD. GII, SGD. GII, 2021)
Ans. Gravitational acceleration: The acceleration of a freely falling bodies is called gravitational acceleration. It is denoted by $\mathbf{g}$.
Value of $\mathbf{g}$ : On the surface of the Earth, the value of $\mathbf{g}$ is approximately $10 \mathrm{~ms}^{-2}$.
⇒ For bodies falling freely g is positive. $\quad \Rightarrow \quad$ For bodies, moving up g is negative. 3. Define uniform acceleration. (GRW. GI, MLN. GI, 2018) (MLN. GII, 2022) (LHR. GI, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, SWL GII, 2023)

Ans. Uniform Acceleration: A body has uniform acceleration if it has equal changes in velocity in equal intervals of time however short the interval may be.
(v) Differentiate between variable and uniform speed. (SGD. Gl, RWP. GI, 2014) (SGD. GI, 2016) (DGK. GI, 2018) (SWL. GI, 2022)

Ans. Variable speed: A body has variable speed if it covers equal distances in unequal intervals of time however short the interval may be.
Uniform Speed: A body has uniform speed if it covers equal distances in equal intervals of time however short the interval may be.

If the speed of the body does not vary and has the same value then the body is said to posses uniform speed. 5. A player covers $\mathbf{8 0 m}$ distance in $\mathbf{1 0}$ seconds.

Find its average speed.
(RWP. GII, 2018)
Ans. Total distance $=80 \mathrm{~m}$
Total time $=10 \mathrm{sec}$
Average speed $=\frac{\text { Total distance }}{\text { Total time }}$
Average speed $=\frac{80}{10}=8 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ 6. Convert $1 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ into $\mathrm{Kmh}^{-1}$. (DGK Gi, 2023)

Ans. $\quad 1 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}=\frac{1 \times 3600}{1000} \mathrm{kmh}^{-1}=3.6 \mathrm{kmh}^{-1}$

## $2.5+2.6+2.7$ Graphical Analysis of Motion + Equations of Motion + Motion of Freely Falling Bodies

1. Draw the graph of constant speed. (GRW. GI, 2016)(BWP. GII, 2017)(SGD. GI. 2021)

Ans. When the speed of the object is constant with time, then the speed-time graph will be a horizontal line parallel to time-axis. 2. Define distance time graph.
(RWP. Gll, 2017)
Ans. It is useful to represent the motion of objects using graphs. The terms
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-13.jpg?height=200&width=240&top_left_y=1414&top_left_x=1259) distance and displacement are used interchangeably when the motion is in a straight line. Similarly if the motion is in a straight line then speed and velocity are also used interchangeably. In a distance-time graph, time is taken along horizontal axis while vertical axis shows the distance covered by the object. 3. What is meant by graph?
(RWP. Gl, 2018)
Ans. Graph is a pictorial way of presenting information about the relation between various quantities. 4. Represent à force of 80 N acting

Sol. towards North of East.
(GRW. GI, 2019)
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-13.jpg?height=233&width=212&top_left_y=1941&top_left_x=126) 5. Define independent variable and dependent variable with respect to graph.(MLN. G. 2023)
Ans. The quantities between which a graph is plotted are called the variables, One of the quantities is called the independent quantity and the other quantity, the value of which varies with the independent quantity is called the dependent quantity. 6. Write three equations of Motion for bodies moving under Gravity.
(BWP. GI, 2019) (FSD. GL, 2023)
Ans.1. $v_{f}=v_{i}+g t$ 2. $h=v_{1} t+\frac{1}{2}+g t^{2}$ 3. $2 g h=v_{f}^{2}-v_{f}^{2}$ 7. What was Galileo's view about freely falling bodies?

Ans. Galileo was the first scientist who, notice that all the freely falling objects have the same acceleration, independent of their masses.

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

2.2. Explain translatory motion and give examples of various types of translatory motion.

Ans. Translatory motion: The motion in which a body moves along a line without any rotation, is called translatory motion.
In translatory motion the line may be straight or curved.
Types of translatory motion: There are three types of translatory motion.
(a) Circular motion
(b) Linear motion
(c) Random motion
(a) Circular motion: The motion of an object in a circular path is known as circular motion.

Examples: (i) A bicycle or a car moving along a circular track.
(ii) The riders in a moving ferris wheel have circular motion.
(b) Linear motion: Straight line motion of a body is known as its linear motion.

Examples: (i) Aeroplane flying straight in air is an example of linear motion
(ii) Objects falling vertically down is an example of linear motion
(c) Random motion: The disordered or irregular motion of an object is called random motion.

Examples: (i) Motion of insects and birds is random motion.
(ii) The motion of dust or smoke particles in the air is random motion.
2.3. Differentiate between the following:
(i) Rest and motion.
(ii) Circular motion and rotatory motion.
(iii) Distance and displacement
(iv) Speed and velocity.
(v) Linear and random motion.
(vi) Scalars and vectors

Ans. (i) Difference between rest and motion:
(GRW. GII, FSD. GI, MLN. GII, SWL GII, DGK. GII, BWP. GI, 2015)

(SWL. GI, RWP. GI \& GII, BWP. GI \& GI, 2016) (MLN. GII. SGD. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2017) (MLN. GII, SGD. GI, BWP. GI, 2018) (MLN. GI, SGD. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, FSD. GI, 2021) (LHR. GI\&GI, GRW. GII, MUN. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2022) (DGK. GII, 2023)
| Rest | Motion |
| :--- | :--- |
| $\Rightarrow$ A body is said to be at rest, if it does not <br> change its position with respect to its <br> surroundings. | $\Rightarrow$A body is said to be in motion, if it <br> changes its position with respect to its <br> surroundings. <br> rest position. |

(ii) Difference between circular motion and rotatory motion:

| Circular Motion                                                                                                                                                                                         | Rotatory Motion                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The motion of an object in a circular path is <br> known as circular motion. <br> Motion of the earth around the sun and <br> motion of the moon around the earth are <br> examples of circular motion. | $\Rightarrow$The spinning motion of a body about its <br> axis is called its rotatory motion. <br> The motion of the Earth about its own axis <br> is rotatory motion. <br> The type of motion of a bicycle wheel <br> about its axis is also rotatory motio |

(iii) Difference between distance and displacement:

| Distance                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Displacement                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| :---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ⇒ Length of a path between two points is called the distance between those points. <br> ⇒ Distance is a scalar quantity because it can be completely described with the help of magnitude only. <br> ⇒ The value of distance can be found out by given formula. $S=v \times t .$ <br> ⇒ In the given figure the distance is represented by $y$.![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-14.jpg?height=129&width=261&top_left_y=2282&top_left_x=293) | ⇒ Displacement is the shortest distance, between two points which has magnitude and direction. <br> ⇒ Displacement is a vector quantity because it can be completely described with the help of magnitude and direction. <br> ⇒ The value of displacement can be derived by given formula, $d=v \times t$ <br> ⇒ In the given figure the displacement is represented by x .![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-14.jpg?height=133&width=208&top_left_y=2282&top_left_x=986) |

(iv) Difference between speed and velocity:
(GRW. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GII, 2017) (RWP. GII, 2018) (RWP. GI, 2019) (SWL. GI, MLN. GI, BWP. GI \& GI, RWP. GI, 2021) (MLN. GI, SGD. GI, DGK, GI, 2023)

| Speed                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Velocity                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| ⇒ The distance covered by an object in unit time is called its speed. <br> ⇒ Speed can be calculated by given formula. $\text { Speed }=\frac{\text { distance covered }}{\text { time }}$ <br> ⇒ Speed is a scalar quantity. Because it can be described completely by a magnitude only. <br> ⇒ A man covers 20 m distance in 5 sec . Its speed is $4 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$. | ⇒ The rate of displacement of a body is called its velocity. <br> ⇒ Velocity can be calculated by given formula. $\text { Velocity }=\frac{\text { displacement }}{\text { time taken }}$ <br> ⇒ Velocity is a vector quantity. Because it can be described completely by a magnitude and direction. <br> ⇒ A man covers 20 m distance in 5 sec towards North. Its velocity is $4 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$ towards north. |

(v) Difference between linear and random motion:
(SWL GI \& GI, 2019)

| Linear motion                                                                                                                                                                   | Random motion                                                                                                                                                       |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| ⇒ Straight line motion of a body is known as its linear motion. <br> ⇒ Aeroplanes flying straight in air and objects falling vertically down are the examples of linear motion. | ⇒ The disordered or irregular motion of an object is called random motion. <br> ⇒ The motion of dust or smoke particles in the air is the example of random motion. |

(vi) Difference between scalars and vectors:
(FSD. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, MLN. GI, 2016) (LHR. GI \& GII, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, 2017)
(SWL GII, RWP. GI \& GI, BWP. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI \& GI, GRW. GI, SWL GI, RWP. GI, 2023)

| Scalars                                                                                                                  |                                                             Vectors                                                              |
| :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------: |
| $\Rightarrow$ A scalar is described completely by its                                                                    |                                        $\Rightarrow$ A vector is described completely by                                         |
| magnitude only. <br> $\Rightarrow$ Mass, length, time, speed, volume, work <br> and energy are some examples of scalars. | $\Rightarrow$magnitude and direction. <br> Velocity, displacement, force, momentum <br> and torque are some examples of vectors. |

### 2.4 Define the terms speed, velocity and acceleration.

Ans. Speed:
(MLN. GI, LHR. GI \& GI, SGD. GI \& GI, BWP. GI, 2015) (MLN. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2016)
⇒ The distance covered by an object in unit time is called speed.
⇒ Speed can be calculated as $v=\frac{S}{t}$
⇒ Unit of speed is metre per second ( $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}$ ). $\quad \Rightarrow \quad$ It is a sealar quantity.
Acceleration:
⇒ Acceleration is defined as the rate of change of velocity of a body.
⇒ Acceleration can be calculated as.

$$
\text { Acceleration }=\frac{\text { Change in velocity }}{\text { time taken }}
$$

⇒ Unit of acceleration is metre per second per second $\left(\mathrm{ms}^{-2}\right) . \quad \Rightarrow \quad$ It is a vector quantity.
Velocity:
⇒ The rate of displacement of a body is called its velocity. Velocity can be calculated as $v=\frac{d}{t}$
⇒ Unit of velocity is metre per second ( $\mathrm{ms}^{-1}$ )
⇒ It is a vector quantity.
2.5: Can a body moving at a constant speed have acceleration?
(LHR. GII, MLN. GII, 2014) (GRW. GII, 2017) (SWL. GI, 2019) (MLN. GII, RWP. GII, 2021) (DGK, GI \& GII, 2022)
Ans. Yes a body moving at a constant speed have acceleration if it changes its direction or moving in a circular path.
2.6: How do riders in a Ferris wheel possess translatory motion but not rotatory motion?

Ans. In circular motion the point about which a body goes around, is outside the body. In rotatory motion the line about which a body moves is passing through the body itself.
Riders in a ferris wheel have rotatory motion because the axis about which a rider moves is passing through the rider itself.
2.7: Sketch a distance-time graph for a body starting from rest. How will you determine the speed of a body from this graph?
Ans.(i) Object is moving with constant speed.'
The speed of an object is said to be constant if it covers equal distances in equal intervals of time. The distance-time graph as shown in figure is a straight line. Its slope gives the speed of the object. Consider two points A and B on the graph:

Speed of the object $=$ Slope of line AB .
Speed of object $=\frac{\text { distance } \mathrm{EF}}{\text { timeCD }}$
Speed of the object $=\frac{20}{10}=2 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$
The speed found from the graph is $2 \mathrm{~ms}^{-1}$.
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-16.jpg?height=239&width=328&top_left_y=115&top_left_x=1083)

Distance-time graph showing constant speed.
(ii) Objective is moving with variable speed:

Ans. When a body is moving with variable speed, the shape of its speed-time graph is not a straight line. 2. What would be the shape of a speed - time graph of a body moving with variable speed?
(LHR. GII, 2015) (DGK. GII, 2019)
Ans. When a body is moving with variable speed, the shape of its speed-time graph is not a straight line.
2.9: Which of the following can be obtained from speed-time graph of a body?
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-16.jpg?height=487&width=672&top_left_y=390&top_left_x=871)
(i) Initial speed.
(ii) Final speed.
(iii) Distance covered in time t.
(iv) Acceleration of motion.

Ans. All the given factors can be obtained from speed-time graph of a moving body.
E.10: How can vector quantities be represented graphically?
(LHR. GI, SWL GII, RWP. GII, 2014)
(SWL GI, 2015)(SWL. GI, SWL. GI, 2016) (SWL GII, 2018)(LHR. GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, DGK. GI \& GII, BWP. GI, 2021) (MLN. GI, 2022)
Ans. Graphically a vector can be represented by a line segment with an arrow head. In the given figure the line AB with arrowhead at B represents a vector $\mathbf{V}$.
The length of the line AB gives the magnitude of the vector $\mathbf{v}$ on a selected scale.
While the direction of the line from $A$ to $B$ gives the direction of the vector $V$.
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-16.jpg?height=169&width=260&top_left_y=1095&top_left_x=1285)

Direction of the line from A to B gives the direction of the vector $\mathbf{V}$.
2.11: Why vector quantities cannot be added and subtracted like scalar quantities?
(RWP. GI, DGK. GII, 2014) (MLN. GII, 2019)
Ans. Scalars quantities are the quantities which can be described completely by magnitude while vectors quantities need direction and magnitude for their complete description.
The quantities having direction cannot be added and subtracted like scalar quantities.
9.2. How are vector quantities important to us in our daily life?
(LHR. GL, 2016)
Ans. Vector quantities are important to us in our daily life because a vector can be described completely by magnitude along with its direction. Examples of vectors are velocity, displacement, force, momentum, torque, etc. It would be meaningless to describe vectors without direction. For example, distance of a place from reference point is insufficient to locate that place. The direction of that place from reference point is also necessary to locate it.
2.13 Derive equations of motion for uniformly accelerated rectilinear motion.,(Subjective type Question)

Ans. For answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
2.1\% Sketch a velocity - time graph for the motion of the body. From the graph explaining each step, calculate total distance covered by the body.
Ans. The area under the velocity -time graph shows the distance covered by a body.
In case of uniform motion, the area of figures formed on graph can be found by suitable formulas:
Velocity-time graph of motion of body: A body is moving in a straight line. The speed time graph of its motion is shown by the figure.
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/80cb1392-8d0d-4a69-9289-370863e9ae76-16.jpg?height=264&width=452&top_left_y=1867&top_left_x=1101)

Total distance covered by a body: The total distance covered by a body can be found by the following method with the help of the given graph.

Total distance coverved $=$ Area under the graph (Trapezium OABC)

Total distance covered

$$
\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{1}{2}(\mathrm{sum} \text { of parallel sides })(\text { height }) \\
& =\frac{1}{2}(18+30)(16)=\frac{1}{2}(48)(16) \\
& =384 \mathrm{~m}
\end{aligned}
$$

(iii) Can a body moving at a constant speed have acceleration?

## Short Questions developed according to the New Examination Techniques <br> (Knowledge, Understanding, Application, Analytical and Conceptual) of the Education Department.

### 3.1 Force, Inertia and Momentum

1. As the card flicks away, the coin falls into the glass. Why?

Ans. The coin falls into the glass due to inertia while the card flicks away. 2. Define momentum and force.
(SGD. GII, 2022)
Ans. Momentum: Momentum of a body is equal to the product of its mass and velocity: Momentum of a body is the quantity of motion possessed by the body.
Force: A force is an agency which moves or tends to move, stop or tends to stop the motion of a body. The force can also change the direction of motion of a body. 3. Differentiate between kinematics and dynamics.
(FSD. GII, 2022)
Ans. Kinematics: Kinematics is the study of motion of an object without discussing the cause of motion.

Dynamics: The branch of mechanics that deals with the study of motion of an object and the causes of its motion is called dynamics.

## $\mathbf{3 . 2} \boldsymbol{+} \mathbf{3 . 3} \boldsymbol{+} \mathbf{3 . 4} \boldsymbol{N} \boldsymbol{e} \mathbf{w t o n}^{\prime} \boldsymbol{s}$ Laws of Motion + Friction + Uniform Circular Motion

1. State Newton's First Law of Motion. (MLN. GI, 2014)(DGK. GI, SGD. GI, SWL. GI, 2015) (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, DGK. GI, 2016)
   (FSD. GII, SWL GI, 2017) (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2018) (SGD. GII, DGK. GI, 2019) (FSD. GII, RWP. GI, 2022) (SGD. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Newton's First Law of Motion: "A body continues its state of rest or of uniform motion in a straight line provided no net force acts on it."
2. Define Newton's third law of motion. Give an example. (SWLGI,2014)(GRW.GI,SWLGII,2015)(RWP.GI,SGD.GI,2016)
   (LHR. GII, 2017) (GRW. GI, FSD. GI, MLN. GI, 2018) (LHR. GII, MLN. GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (BWP. GI, 2022) (LHR. GII, FSD. GII, 2023)
   Ans. Newton's third law of motion: "To every action there is always an equal but opposite reaction."
   Example: The weight of the book lying on the table is acting on the table in the downward direction. This is the action. The reaction of the table acts on the book in the upward direction.
3. What is the relation between force and momentum?
   (SGD. GII, 2016) (BWP. GI, 2022)
   Ans. When a force acts on a body, it produces acceleration in the body and will be equal to the rate of change of momentum of the body. We can write it as;
   Change in momentum $=$ final momentum - initial momentum
   $P_{f}-P_{i}=m v_{f}-m v_{i}$
   Thus, rate of change in momentum is given by.
   $\frac{P_{\mathrm{f}}-P_{\mathrm{i}}}{t}=m\left(\frac{v_{\mathrm{f}}-v_{\mathrm{i}}}{t}\right)$
   as, $\quad \frac{V_{f}-V_{i}}{t}=a$
   So, $-\frac{P_{f}-P_{i}}{t}=m a$.
   and Newton's second law of motion tells us that;
   F = ma
   By putting the value of F in eq. (I)
   $\frac{P_{f}-P_{i}}{t}=F$ which is the required relation.
4. Define weight and write its unit.
   (MLN. GI, 2017)
   Ans. Weight of the body is equal to the force with which Earth attracts it. Weight is a vector quantity.
   Unit: The SI unit of weight is newton (N).
5. The weight of a body is 147 N . What is its mass (Take value of g is $10 \mathrm{~ms}^{-2}$ )?
   (DGK. GII, 2017) (RWP. GII, 2018)
   Data: Weight

$$
=\mathrm{w}=147 \mathrm{~N}
$$

Gravitational acceleration $=\mathrm{g}=10 \mathrm{~ms}^{-2}$
To find out:

$$
\begin{aligned}
& \text { Mass }=m=? \\
& w \quad=m g
\end{aligned}
$$

Formula:
By putting values, we get:

$$
\begin{aligned}
& \mathrm{m}=\frac{w}{g} \\
& \mathrm{~m}=\frac{147}{10} \\
& \mathrm{~m}=14.7 \mathrm{~kg}
\end{aligned}
$$

Ans. The required mass of the body is 14.7 kg . 6. Define force and write the name of its unit.
(BWP. GII, MLN. GII, 2017) (MLN. GII, 2022)
(MLN. GII, GRW. GI \& GII, SGD. GI, BWP. GI \& GI, 2018) (DGK. GI, MLN. GI, BWP. GI, 2019)
Ans. A force is a push or pull. It moves or tends to move, stops or tends to stop the motion of a body.
Unit: The SI unit of force is Newton (N). 7. Define mass and write its unit in SI.
(DGK. Gl, 2019)
Ans. Mass of a body is the quantity of matter possessed by the body. It is a scalar quantity.
SI unit of mass is kilogramme. 8. Define friction and limiting friction.

Ans. Friction: The force that opposes the motion of moving objects is called friction.
i.e. $\quad \mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{S}}=\mu \mathrm{R}$
Limiting friction: Friction is equal to the applied force that tends to move a body at rest. It increases with the applied force friction has a maximum value. It does not increase beyond this. The maximum value of friction is known as the force of limiting friction $\mathrm{F}_{3(\max )}$. It depends upon the normal reaction (processing force) between the two surfaces in contact.

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

3.2: Define the following terms:
(i) Inertia
(ii) Momentum
(iii) Force
(iv) Force $\mathrm{e}^{-}$friction
(v) Centripetal force

Ans. (i) Inertia: Int ${ }^{c}$ a body is its property due to which it resists any change in its state of rest or motion.
(ii) Momentum: Momes. a of a body is the quantity of motion possessed by the body. Momentum of a body is equal to the product of its mass and velocity.
(iii) Force: A force is a push or pull. It moves or tends to move, stops or tends to stop the motion of a body. The force can also change the direction of motion of a body.
(iv) Force of Friction: A force between the sliding objects which opposes the relative motion between them is called force of friction.

The force that opposes the motion of moving objects is called friction.
(v) Centripetal force: The force which keeps the body to move in a circular path is called the centripetal force.

$$
\mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{c}}=\frac{\mathrm{mv}^{2}}{\mathrm{r}}
$$

3.3: What is the difference between?
(i) Mass and weight (LHR. GII, MLN.GII, SGD. GI, 2014) (SGD. GII, SWL' GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GI, 2015)
(FSD. GII, DGK GII, 2016) (SWL GI, SGD. GI, BWP. GI, 2017) (LHR. GII, SWL GII, RWP. GI \& GII, DGK. GII, BWP. GI, 2018) (GRW. GII, FSD. GH, SWL. GII, 2019) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GII, RWP. GII, 2022) (GRW. GI, MLN. GI \& GHI, SWL GII, SGD. GII, RWP. GII, 2023)
(ii) Action and reaction
(DGK. GI, 2018) (BWP. Gl, 2021)
(iii) Sliding friction and rolling friction
(SWL GII, 2014) (FSD. GIL, RWP. GII, 2015) (RWP. GII, 2017)
(GRW. GII, 2018) (RWP. GII, DGK. GII, 2019) (GRW. GI, 2011)
Ans. (i) Difference between mass and weight:

| Mass | Weight |
| :--- | :----- |
| 四   | 面     |

(ii) Difference between action and reaction:

| Action                                                                                              |                                                       Reaction                                                       |
| :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------: |
| It is a force that is exerted by a body <br> let A on the other body B is called <br> action force. | It is also a force which is exerted by the <br> second body let B on the first body A is <br> called reaction force. |

(iii) Difference between sliding friction and rolling friction:

| Sliding friction                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Rolling friction                                                                |
| :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| ![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/3d3e96ea-86fe-49f4-965d-460dafbcf27c-22.jpg?height=50&width=43&top_left_y=2146&top_left_x=143) <br> A force between the sliding objects which opposes the relative motion between them is called sliding friction.![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/3d3e96ea-86fe-49f4-965d-460dafbcf27c-22.jpg?height=45&width=41&top_left_y=2289&top_left_x=143) | The magnitude of sliding friction is very large as compare to rolling friction. |

3.4: What is the law of Inertia?

Ans. Newton's first law of motion deals with the inertial property of matter, so Newton's first law of motion is also known as law of inertia.
Statement: A body continues its state of rest or of uniform motion in a straight line provided no net force acts on it.'
3.5. Why is it dangerous to travel on the roof of a bus?
(FSD. GI, DGK. GII, 2019)
Ans. If a person travels on the roof of a bus, it would be dangerous because when a bus takes a sharp turn, passengers falls in the outward direction. It is due to inertia that they want continue their motion in a straight line and thus fall outwards.
3.6: Why does a passenger move outward when a bus takes a turn?
(GRW. GII, MLN. GI, 2011)
Ans. When \& bus takes a sharp turn, passengers fall in the outward direction. It is due to inertia that they want to continue their motion in a straight line and thus fall outwards
3.7: How can you relate a force with the change of momentum of a body?

Ans. When a force acts on a body, it produces acceleration in the body and will be equal to the rate of change of momentum of the body. We can write it as;
Change in momentum = final momentum - initial momentum
$P_{f}-P_{i}=m v_{f}-m v_{i}$
Thus, rate of change in momentum is given by.
$\frac{P_{\mathrm{f}}-P_{\mathrm{i}}}{\mathrm{t}}=\mathrm{m}\left(\frac{\mathrm{v}_{\mathrm{f}}-\mathrm{v}_{\mathrm{i}}}{\mathrm{t}}\right)$
as, $\frac{v_{f}-v_{i}}{t}=a$
So, $\quad \frac{P_{f}-P_{i}}{t}=m a$.
and Newton's second law of motion tells us that;
$\mathrm{F}=\mathrm{ma}$
By putting the value of F in eq. (I)
$\frac{P_{\mathrm{f}}-P_{\mathrm{i}}}{\mathrm{t}}=F$
which is the required relation.
3.8. What will be the tension in a rope that is pulled from its ends by two opposite forces 100 N each?
(SWL. GII, 2014)
Ans. The total tension in the rope will be:
$\mathrm{T}=100 \mathrm{~N}$
3.9: Action and reaction are always equal and opposite. Then how does a body move? (SWL G. 2019)

Ans. According to Newton's third law of motion, action and reaction are always equal and opposite in direction. But action and reaction forces always act on different bodies, so they do not cancel the effect of each other, and under this condition of forces the body moves irrespective to this, that action and reaction are equal but opposite in direction.
3.10: A horse pulls the cart. If the action and reaction are equal and opposite then how does the cart move?
Ans. As a horse pulls the cart, it is the action of the horse on the Eart, according to Newton's third law of motion, Eart also applies the equal amount of force as a reaction on the horse in opposite direction. This would be cancelled out, if both the forces act on one body, but these two forces act on two separate bodies so they would not cancel the effect of each other and the cart moves.

### 3.11: What is the law of conservation of momentum?

(MLN. GI, BWP. GII, 2014) (FSD. GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GII, 2015) (MLN. GII, DGK. GII, 2017)
(SGD. GII, 2018) (FSD. GII, MLN. GII, SWL. GII, 2019) (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, MLN. GII, 2022) (RWP. GII, 2023)
Ans. The momentum of an isolated system of two or more than two interacting bodies before and after the collisions remains the same is known as law of conservation of momentum. Let two bodies of
masses $\mathrm{m}_{1}$ and $\mathrm{m}_{2}$ moving with velocities $\mathrm{v}_{1}$ and $\mathrm{v}_{2}$ respectively before collision and their velocities after collision become $\mathrm{u}_{1}$ and $\mathrm{u}_{2}$ respectively. According to the statement of law of conservation of momentum.

$$
m_{1} v_{1}+m_{2} v_{2}=m_{1} u_{1}+m_{2} u_{2}
$$

3.12: Why is the law of conservation of momentum important?

Ans. Law of conservation of momentum is very much important because it is applicable on all objects in the universe either larger or smaller. This law has vast applications. According to this law the momentum of an isolated system of two or more than two interacting bodies remains same.

### 3.13: When a gun is fired, it recoils. Why?

(RWP. GII, BWP. GI, 2014) (MLN. GI, FSD. GI, 2015) (LHR. GI, 2018)
(GRW. GI, FSD. GI, 2019) (SWL GII, 2021) (FSD. GI, SWL GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)
Ans. Consider a system of gun and a bullet. Before firing the gun, both the gun and bullet are at rest, so the total momentum of the system is zero. As the gun is. fired, bullet shoots out of the gun and acquires momentum. To conserve momentum of the system, the gun recoils. According to law of conservation of momentum, the total momentum of the gun and the bullet will also be zero after the gun is fired. Therefore the gun recoils.

### 3.14 Describe two situations in which force of friction is needed.

(SWL GI, 2014) (MLN. GI, GRW. GI, SGD. GI, 2015) (RWP. GII, MLN. GI, 2016) (DGK. GII, 2019)
Ans. There are many conditions in which friction is desirable, two of them-is given below:
(i) Friction is needed when we write, we cannot write if there would be no friction between the paper and the pencil.
(ii) Friction enables us to walk on the ground, we cannot run on slippery ground. A slippery ground offers very little friction. Hence, any body who tries to run on a slippery ground may meet an accident.
3.15: How does oiling the moving parts of a machine lowers friction.
(GRW. GII, 2017) (FSD. GI, 2019)
Ans. By making the sliding surfaces as smooth as possible we can reduce the friction and for this, we apply any lubricant such as oil in the moving parts of machine. It will smooth the surfaces which are sliding and hence reduces the friction between these parts of a machine.

### 3.16: Describe ways to reduce friction.

(MLN. GII, 2015) (SWL. GI, BWP. GI \& GII, 2016) (RWP. GI, 2017)
(FSD. GII, SWL. GII, 2018) (LHR. GI, GRW. G \& GII, 2019) (SWL. GI, MLN. GII, DGK. GI, RWP. GI, 2021) (SGD. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, 2023)
Ans. The friction can be reduced by:
(i) making the sliding surfaces as smooth as possible.
(ii) making the fast moving objects a streamline shape (fish shape) such as cars, trains and aeroplanes. This causes the smooth flow of air around their bodies and thus minimizes air resistance at high speeds.
(iii) using lubricants between the sliding surfaces.
(iv) using ball bearings or roller bearings. Because rolling friction is much less than sliding friction.
3.17: Why rolling friction is less than sliding friction?
(LHR. GII, DGK. GII, BWP. GII, 2014)
(BWP. GI, 2015) (DGK GI, 2016) (LHR. GI, 2018) (LHR. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GI, SGD. GI \& GI, RWP. GI, 202I) (GRW. GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)
Ans. All surfaces have pits and bumps and when two such surfaces are in contact. Then contact points between the two surfaces form a sort of cold welds. These cold welds resist the surfaces from sliding over each other. More is the area of in contact surfaces more would be the friction. In sliding friction more area is in contact. For example, when the axel of wheel is pushed, the force of friction between the wheel and the ground at the point of contact provides the reaction force. The reaction force acts at the contact points of the wheel in a direction opposite to the applied force. The wheel rolls with out rupturing the cold welds. That is why the rolling friction is extremely small than sliding friction.
3.18: What you know about the following:
(i) Tension in a string.
(ii) Limiting force of friction
(iii) Braking force
(iv) Skidding of vehicles (v) Seatbelts
(vi) Banking of roads
(vii) Cream separator

Ans. (i) Tension in a string: Consider a block supported by a string. The upper end of the string is
fixed on a stand. Let w be the weight of the block. The block pulls the string downwards by its weight. This causes a tension " T " in the string. The tension T in the string is acting upwards at the block. As the block is at rest, therefore, the weight of the block acting downwards must be balanced by the upwards tension T in the string. Thus the tension T in the string must be equal and opposite to the weight w of the body.
(ii) Limiting force of friction:

Friction is equal to the applied force that tends to move a body at rest. It increases with the applied force friction has a maximum value. It does not increase beyond this. The maximum value of friction is known as the force of limiting friction ( $\mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{s}}$ ). It depends upon the normal reaction (processing force) between the two surfaces in contact. And mathematically.
$\mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{s}}=\mu \mathrm{R}$
where co-efficient of friction $=\mu$
$\mathrm{R}=$ normal reaction
$\mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{S}}=$ force of limiting friction
(iii) Braking force:

To stop a car quickly, a large force of friction between the tyres and the road is needed. But there is a limit to this force of friction that tyres can provide. If the brakes are applied too strongly, the wheels of the car will lock up (stop turning) and the car will skid due to its large momentum. It will lose its directional control that may result in an accident. In order to reduce the chance of skidding, it is advisable not to apply brakes too hard that lock up their rolling motion especially at high speeds. Force exerted by brakes is called braking force.
(iv) Skidding of vehicles:

To stop a car or vehicle quickly, a large force of friction between the tyres and the roads is needed. But there is a limit to this force of friction that tyres can provide. If the brakes are applied too strongly, the wheels of the car will lock up (stop turning) and the car will skid due to its large momentum. Its directional control will be lost and it would meet an accident. In order to reduce the chance of skidding, it is advisable not to apply brakes too hard that lock up their rolling motion especially at high speed. Moreover it is unsafe to drive a vehicle with worn out tyres.
(v) Seat belts:

In case of an accident, a person not wearing seatbelt will continue moving until stopped suddenly by something before him. This something may be a windscreen, another passenger or back of the seat in the front of him. Seatbelts are useful in two ways.
(1) They provide an external force to a person wearing seat belt.
(2) The additional time is required for stretching seat belts. This prolongs the stopping time for momentum to change and reduces the effect of collision.

## (vi) Banking of the roads:

When a car takes a turn, centripetal force is needed to keep it in its curved track. The friction between the tyres and the road provides the necessary centripetal force. The car would skid if the force friction between the tyres and the road is not sufficient enough particularly when the roads are wet. This problem is solved by banking of curved roads. Banking of a road means that the outer edge of a road is raised. Imagine a vehicle on a curved road. Banking causes a component of vehicle's weight to provide the necessary centripetal force while taking a turn. Thus banking of roads prevents skidding of vehicle and thus makes the driving safe.
(vii) Cream separator:

Most modern plants use a separator to control the fat contents of various products. A separator is a high-speed spinner. It acts on the same principle of centrifuge machines. The bowl spins at very high speed causing the heavier contents of milk to move outward in the bowl pushing the lighter contents inward towards the spinning axis. Cream or butterfat is lighter than other components in milk. Therefore, skimmed milk, which is denser than cream is collected at the outer wall of the
bowl. The lighter part (cream) is pushed towards the centre from where it is collected through a pipe.
3.19: What would happen if all friction suddenly disappears?

Ans. It there was no friction then we could not walk on the ground. Noting would be steady on the ground and it would be nearly impossible to keep things still as there would be no force to oppose an object motion. Every thing would be slide around would not be stopped. There would be no sound because the waves have to be transferred with air friction, many things would be just sliding and sliding. Infact, noting would exist in universe, without friction.
3.208 Why the spinner of a washing machine is made to spin at a very high speed?
(BWP. GII, 2016)
Ans. Spinner of a washing machine is made to spin at a very high speed. Because when it spins at high speed, the water from wet clothes is forced out through these holes due to lack of centripetal force.

(SWL Gl, 2014)
(LHR. GII, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2015) (MLN. GI, SGD. GI, BWP. GI, 2016) (RWP. GI, 2017) (LHR. GI \& GI, SWL GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2018) (GRW, GII, MLN, GII, BWP. GI, 2019) (FSD. GII, MLN. GI \& GII, DGK. GI \& GI, BWP. GI \& GI, 202I)
(GRW. GI \& GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI \& GI, DGK. GI \& GI, 2023)
(a) 2
(b) 3
(c) 4
(d) Any number
iii. The number of perpendicular components of a force are:
(GRW. GII, FSD. GII, 2014) (GRW. GII, SGD. GII, DGK. GII, 2015) (LHR. GI, FSD. GI, RWP. GII, 2016) (MLN. GI, SWL. GI, SGD. GI \& GI, 2017) (SGD. GI, BWP. GII, 2018) (LHR. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI \& GII, GRW. GI, SGD. GI, 2021) (LHR. GII, SWL GI, BWP. GII, 2022) (MLN. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2023)
(a) 1
(b) 2
(c) 3
(d) 4
iv. A force of 10 N is making an angle of $30^{\circ}$ with the horizontal. Its horizontal component will be:
(FSD. GII, DGK. GI, 2014) (SWL. GII, RWP. GI \& GII, 2015) (LHR. GII, BWP. GII, SGD. GI, 2016) (MLN. GI, RWP. GI, 2018)
(MLN. Gl, SWL GII, SGD. GI, 2019) (RWP. GI, 2021) (LHR. GI, MLN. GII, SWL. GI, SGD. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, FSD. GII, SWL GI, SGD. GI, BWP. GI \& GI, 2023)
(a) 4 N
(b) 5 N
(c) 7 N
(d) 8.7 N
v. A couple is formed by:
(SGD. Gll, 2014)
(a) two forces perpendicular to each other
(b) two like parallel forces
(c) two equal and opposite forces in the same line
(d) two equal and opposite forces not in the same line

(MLN. GII, SGD. GII, 2014) (LHR. GI, 2015) (LHR. GI, DGK. GII, 2017) (SGD. GI, 2021)
(a) acceleration is uniform
(b) speed is uniform
(c) speed and acceleration are uniform
(d) acceleration is zero

(RWP. GII, FSD. GI, 2014)(BWP. GI, 2017)(FSD. GI, 2019)

(b) is at the lowest position
(c) keeps its height if displaced
(d) is situated at its bottom
viii. Racing cars are made stable by:
(GRW. GI, BWP. GI, SWL GII, 2014) (SGD. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GI, 2015)
(GRW. GI, MLN. GI, SWL GII, 2016) (SWL GII, RWP. GI, 2018) (SWL. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)
(a) increasing their speed
(b) decreasing their mass
(c) lowering their centre of gravity
(d) decreasing their width

## Answers

i. a couple
ii. any number
iii. 2 iv. 8.7 N
v. two equal and opposite forces not in the same line vi. acceleration is zero
vii. keeps its height if displaced viii. lowering their centre of gravity
