1. Define parallel forces. Write the names of its types.

Ans. The forces which are parallel to each other are called parallel forces.
(BWP. GII, 2017) There are two types of parallel forces.
(1) Like parallel forces
(2) Unlike parallel forces 2. What is resultant force? (SWL. GI. SGD. GII, 2018)/GRW. GII, 2019) (LHR. GII, SGD. GII, 2021) (GRW. GI, 2022) (SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2023)

Ans. Resultant force: A resultant force is a single force that has the same effect as the combined effect of all the forces to be added. 3. Differentiate between line of action of force and moment arm.
(FSD. GII, 2021)
Ans. Line of action of force: The line along which a force acts is called the line of action of the force.

Moment arm: The perpendicular distance between the axis of rotation and the line of action of the force is called the moment arm of the force.
Moment arm is represented by distance (L) 4. Define like parallel forces and moment arm.
(DGK. Gl, 2021)
Ans. Like parallel forces are the forces that are paraliel to each other and have the same direction.
Moment arm: The perpendicular distance between the axis of rotation and the line of action of the force is called the moment arm of the force.
Moment arm is represented by distance (L). 5. Define torque and moment arm.
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/c3f63ea7-de82-42e6-93e1-49ca9c25de57-31.jpg?height=91&width=520&top_left_y=375&top_left_x=1048&polygon=514,0,518,1,520,3,520,62,518,66,516,68,483,72,127,91,112,91,4,87,2,85,0,70,0,5,2,3,22,1,119,0)
(FSD. GII, 2019) (LHR. GI, 2022)

Ans. Torque: The turning effect of the forces is called the torque. $\tau=F \times I$
Moment arm: The perpendicular distance between the axis of rotation and the line of action of force.
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/c3f63ea7-de82-42e6-93e1-49ca9c25de57-31.jpg?height=124&width=858&top_left_y=558&top_left_x=199)

## What is meant by rigid body?

(FSD. GI \& GII, DGK GI, 2017) (DGK. GII, 2018) (GRW. GI, SWL GII, 2019)
(GRW. GI, SWL GI, 2019) (BWP. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2021) (SWL GII, RWP. GI, 2022)(RWP. GI, 2023)
Ans. Rigid Body: A rigid body is the one that is not deformed by force or forces acting on it. 2. Define rigid body and moment arm.
(MLN. GI, 2018)(SGD. GII, 2021) (MLN. GI, 2022)
Ans. Rigid body: A rigid body is the one that is not deformed by force or forces acting on it.
Moment arm: The perpendicular distance between the axis of rotation and the line of action of force.

## 3.

## Define axis of rotation.

(SGD. GII, 2014) (RWP. GI, 2015) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GI, 2017)
(GRW. GII, 2018) (SGD.GII, 2019) (BWP. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2021) (SGD. GI, 2022)
Ans. Axis of rotation: Consider a rigid body. As it rotates, its particles move in fixed circles. A fixed line that passes through the centres of these circles is called axis of rotation of the body. 4. Write the mathematical forms of conditions of torque.

Ans. The torque of force depends upon force $F$ and moment arm i.e.
Torque:

$$
\tau=\mathrm{F} \times \mathrm{L}
$$

5. Define rigid body and line of action of force.
   ![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/c3f63ea7-de82-42e6-93e1-49ca9c25de57-31.jpg?height=256&width=230&top_left_y=1000&top_left_x=1269)
   ${ }^{+}$Finst 3 Nunericuly
   (LHR GI, 2017)

Ans. Rigid body: A rigid body is the one that is not deformed by force or forces acting on it.
Line of action of force:
The line along which a force acts is called the line of action of the force.

## $\mathbf{4 . 7}+\mathbf{4 . 8}+\mathbf{4 . 9}$ Centre of Gravity + Couple + Equilibrium

1. Define the Centre of gravity. (GRW. GI, 2018) (BWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI, 2021) (SWL. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, BWP. GL, 2023)

Ans. Centre of gravity: The centre of gravity of a body is defined as a point where the whole weight of the body appears to act vertically downward. 2. Explain couple with the help of an example.
(SWL. GII, RWP. GII, 2015) (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, SGD. GI, 2016)
(SWL GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2017) (FSD. GI, RWP. GI \& GII, 2019) (MLN. GI, SWL. GI, 2023)
Ans. Couple: A couple is formed by two unlike parallel forces of the same magnitude but not along the same line.
Example: When a driver turns a vehicle, he applies forces that produce a torque. This torque turns the steering wheel. These forces act on opposite sides of the steering wheel as shown in figure. These forces are equal in magnitude but opposite in direction. These two forces form a couple. 3.

Differentiate between Torque and Couple.
(FSD. GII, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, SWL. GI, 2013)
Ans.

| Torque                                                                                                                                                                | Couple                                                                                                        |
| :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| The turning effect fa force is called torque or <br> moment of the force. torque of a force is equal to <br> the product of force and movement arm of the <br> force. | A couple is formed by two unlike parallel forces <br> of the same magnitude but not along the same <br> line. |

4. Write down two conditions of equilibrium.

Ans. First condition of equilibrium: A body is said to satisfy first condition for equilibrium if the resultant of all the forces acting on it is zero.i.e. $\Sigma F=0$
Second condition of equilibrium: A body satisfies second condition of equilibrium when the resultant torque acting on it is zero. i.e. $\Sigma \tau=0$

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

4.2: Define the following:
(i) Resultant vector
(ii) Torque
(iii) Centre of mass
(iv) Centre of gravity

Ans. (i) Resultant vector: A resultant vector is a single vector that has the same effect as the combined effect of all the vectors to be added.
(ii) Torque: The turning effect of a force is called torque or moment of the force. It is determined by the product of force F and its moment arm L . It is denoted as $\tau$. In SI units, the unit of torque is Newton-meter (Nm).
(iii) Centre of mass: Centre of mass of a system is such a point where an applied force causes the system to move without rotation.
(iv) Centre of gravity: The centre of gravity of a body is defined as a point where the whole weight of the body appears to act vertically downward.
4.3: Differentiate the following:
(i) Like and unlike forces
(ii) Torque and couple
(iii) Stable and neutral equilibrium

Ans. (i) Difference between like and unlike forces: (FSD. GI, SWL GI, RWP. GI, 2018) (LHR. GI, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, MLN. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, SWL. GI, BWP. GI, DGK. GII, RWP. GI \& GI, 2021) (LHR. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GII, 2022) (LHR. GI, RWP. GI, 2023)

## Like Forces

i. Like forces are also called like parallel force
ii. Like force are the forces that have the same direction to each other.
iii. A bag has a large number of apples in it, the weight of all the apples is acted vertically downward so these all forces are in same direction, called like forces.

![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/c3f63ea7-de82-42e6-93e1-49ca9c25de57-32.jpg?height=327&width=271&top_left_y=1363&top_left_x=343)
Weight of each apple Like parallel forces

## Unlike Forces

i. Unlike forces are also called unlike parallel forces.
ii. Unlike forces are the forces that are in the opposite direction to each other.
iii. An apple is suspended by a string. The string is stretched by the weight of apple. Weight is acted downward but tension in the string is actedc in upward direction. These are unlike forces.

![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/c3f63ea7-de82-42e6-93e1-49ca9c25de57-32.jpg?height=337&width=247&top_left_y=1392&top_left_x=1031)
Unlike parallel forces along the same line

(ii) Difference between torque and couple:

| Torque                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Couple                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| i. The turning effect of a force is called torque or moment of force <br> ii. To produce a torque we need only one force atleast. <br> iii. The torque is produced by a force F and the moment arm. <br> iv. Torque by a force is the product of force F and its moment arm. | i. A couple is formed by two unlike parallel forces of the same magnitude but not along the same line. <br> ii. To produce a couple we need two unlike parallel forces atleast. <br> iii. Torque of the couple $=\mathrm{F} \times \mathrm{AB}$ in this F represents force and AB represents the distance between two forces. The torque produced by a couple force F and F separated by the total distance (AB), that is the couple arm. <br> iv. The torque of a couple is given by the product of one of the two forces and the perpendicular distance between them. |

(iii) Difference between stable and neutral equilibrium:
(MLN. GI, 2014) (SWL GI, 2015) (GRW. GI \& GI, 2017) (SGD. GI, MLN. GII, RWP. GI, 2016) (GRW. GI, 2018) (SWL GI, 2023)

| Stable equilibrium                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Neutral equilibrium                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| :----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| i. A body is said to be in stable equilibrium if after a slight tilt it returns to its previous position. <br> ii. When a body is in stable equilibrium, its centre of gravity is at the lowest position. When it is tilted, its centre of gravity rises. It returns to its stable state by lowering its centre of gravity. <br> iii. A book placed on the table horizontally is an éxample of stable equilibrium. | i. If a body remains in its new position when disturbed from its previous, it is said to be in a state of neutral equilibrium. <br> ii. In neutral equilibrium, the centre of gravity of the body remains at the same height, irrespective to its new position. <br> iii. The rolling ball is an example of neutral equilibrium. |

4.4. How head to tail rule helps to find the resultant of forces? (Subjective Type Question)
(DGK. GI, 2016) (RWP. GII, 2017) (SGD. GI, 2019) (GRW. GI, BWP. GII, 2021)
Ans. For Answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
4.5: How can a force be resolved into its perpendicular components? (Subjective Type Question)
Ans. For Answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
4.6. When a body is said to be in equilibrium?
(MLN. GI, SGD. GI, 2014) (LHR. GII, 2016) (RWP. GII, 2017) (GRW. GII, MLN. GI, BWP. GI \& GII, 2021) (GRW. GI, 2022)
Ans. A body is said to be in equilibrium if it follows both conditions of equilibrium.
A body is in equilibrium if net force acting on it is zero, and a body is said to be in equilibrium if the resultant torque acting on it is zero.

$$
\begin{aligned}
& \Sigma \mathrm{F}=0, \text { or } \Sigma \mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{y}}=0, \Sigma \mathrm{~F}_{\mathrm{x}}=0 \\
& \Sigma \tau=0
\end{aligned}
$$

4.7: Explain the first condition for equilibrium. (Subjective Type Question)
(MLN. GI \& GII, SGD. GI \& GII, BWP. GII, DGK. GI, RWP. GI \& GI, 2016) (MLN. GI, DGK. GI, 2017) (SGD. GI, 2019)
(LHR. GII, GRW. GI, SWL GII, DGK. GII, SGD. GI, RWP. GI \& GII, 2021) (BWP. GI, 2022)
Ans. For Answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
4.8. Why is there a need of second condition for equilibrium if a body satisfies first condition for equilibrium?
(MLN. GI \& GII, SGD. GI \& GII, BWP. GII, DGK. GI, RWP. GI, 2016) (FSD. GI, 2022)
Ans. The first condition for equilibrium does not ensure that a body is in equilibrium. Consider a body pulled by the forces $\mathrm{F}_{1}$ and $\mathrm{F}_{2}$,
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/c3f63ea7-de82-42e6-93e1-49ca9c25de57-33.jpg?height=176&width=655&top_left_y=1492&top_left_x=851)
the two forces are equal but opposite to each other. These forces are not acted along the same line as given in figure.

The first condition of equilibrium is although satisfied but the body has tendency to rotate. This situation demands another condition for equilibrium that is the second condition of equilibrium, a body satisfies second condition of equilibrium when the resultant torque acting on it zero. $\Sigma \tau=0$
4.9. What is second condition for equilibrium? (Subjective Type Questions)
(SGD. GI, BWP. GI, 2014) (LHR. GI, BWP, GI, 2016) (GRW. GII, SGD. GI, 2017) (LHR. GI, DGK. GI, 2018)(MLN. GI, 2021) (GRW. GI, SGD. GI, 2022)
Ans. For Answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
4.10: Give an example of a moving body which is in equilibrium.
(GRW. GII, 2021)
Ans. A paratrooper coming down with terminal velocity (constant velocity) is in equilibrium as all the forces acting on it is equal to zero, which satisfies the first condition of equilibrium.
4.11: Think of a body which is at rest but not in equilibrium.
(LHR. GII, 2016) (FSD. GII, 2021) (BWP. GII, 2022)
Ans. There is not a single body in the universe which is at rest but not in equilibrium.
4.12: Why cannot a body be in equilibrium due to single force acting on it?
(BWP. Gl, 2014) (LHR. Gl. 2015) (DGK. Gll, 2016)
Ans. For a body is said to be in equilibrium it is necessary that the net force acting on a body is zero and the sum of all the torques acting on a body is zero. These two conditions can not be satisfied
if there is one force only. Because there is not any other force which nullify the effect of this force to keep the body in equilibrium and hence, this single force tends to move or rotate the body according to its point of application. So, if a single force is applied on a body, it could not be in equilibrium i.e

$$
\begin{array}{ll}
\Sigma \mathrm{F} \neq & 0 \\
\Sigma \tau \neq & 0
\end{array}
$$

4.13: Why the height of vehicles is kept as low as possible?
(FSD. GI, SGD. GI, 2014) (SWL GI, 2015) (SWLGII, 2016) (SGD. GI, 2017)
(FSD. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GII, 2019) (MLN. GI \& GII, SGD. GII, 2022) (FSD. GI, 2013)
Ans. Vehicles are made heavy at the bottom and their height is kept to be minimum. This lowers their centre of gravity and helps to increase their stability. Because to make them stable, their centre of mass must be kept as low as possible. Therefore, height of vehicles is kept as low as possible.
4.18 Explain what is meant by stable, unstable and neutral equilibrium. Give one example in each case. (Subjective Type Questions)
Ans. For Answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".

## Unit 04:

Turning Effect of Forces

SUBJECTIVE TYPE (PART - I)

Maximum Marks: 48
Time Allowed : 1.45 Hours

## $5.2+5.3+5.4$ Mass of the Earth + Variation of g with Altitude + Artificial Satellites

1. Write down the value of " $G$ " and mass of earth with SI units.
   (SGD. GI, 2022)
   Ans. Mass of Earth $=6 \times 10^{24} \mathrm{~kg}$

$$
\mathrm{G}=6.673 \times 10^{-11} \mathrm{Nm}^{2} \mathrm{~kg}^{-2}
$$

2. What is difference between ' g ' and ' G '?
   (RWP. GI, 2018) (LHR. GII, 2019) (GRW. GII, 2021)
   Ans.

| $\mathbf{g}$                                                                                                                                                                                                | $\mathbf{G}$                                                                                                                                                                |
| :---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The acceleration of a freely falling bodies is <br> called gravitational acceleration. It is denoted <br> by g. On the surface of the Earth, the value of g g <br> is approximately $10 \mathrm{~ms}^{-2}$. | G is called the universal constant of gravitation. <br> In SI units its value $6.673 \times 10^{-11} \mathrm{Nm}^{2} \mathrm{~kg}^{-2}$. Its <br> value is same everywhere. |

## 3. Define Satellites.

(BWP. GI, 2019) (GRW. GI, MLN. GI, BWP. GI \& GI, 2021) (MLN. GI, BWP. GI, 2023)
Ans. An object that revolves around a planet is called a satellite.
Example: Communication satellites.

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

5.2: What is meant by the force of gravitation?
(SGD. Gl \& GII, DGK, GI, 2014)
(LHR. GI \& GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GII, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2015) (LHR. GI \& GII, FSD. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2016)
(LHR. GI, MLN. GI, RWP. GII, BWP. GI \& GII, 2017) (FSD. GI \& GI, SWL GI \& GII, RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2018) (FSD. GII, BWP. GI, 2019)
(LHR. GII, GRW, GI, MLN. GI, BWP. GI \& GII, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, 2021) (MLN. GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, DGK, GI \& GI, 2023)
Ans. The force due to which every body of the universe attracts every other body is called force of gravitation.
5.3: Do you attract the Earth or the Earth attracts you? Which one is attracting with a larger force? You or the Earth.
Ans. Yes we attracts the Earth or Earth attracts us. Our body is very small, as compared to Earth so, we attract the Earth with a very small and insignificant force. Therefore it is not felt by us.
Earth because of its larger mass attracts us with a larger and significant force.

## 5.4: What is a field force?

(SGD. GII, 2014)(MLN. GII, RWP. GI, 2015)(SWL. GII, DGK. GII, 2016)
(GRW. GI \& FSD. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GII, 2017) (GRW. GI \& GI, SGD. GI, DGK GI, 2018)
(LHR. GI, SGD. GII, 2019) (SWL. GI, 2021) (FSD. GI, SWL GH, 2022)
Ans. The weight of a body is due to the gravitational force with which the Earth attracts a body. Gravitational force is a non-contact force. For example, the velocity of a body, thrown up, goes on decreasing while on return its velocity goes on increasing. This is due to the gravitational pull of the Earth acting on the body whether the body is in contact with the Earth or not. Such a force is called the field force.
5.5: Why earlier scientists could not guess about the gravitational force?

Ans. The first man who came up with the idea of gravity was Isaac Newton. It was an evening of 1665 , when he was trying to solve the mystery why planets revolve around the Sun. Before this, people were not familier even with the word gravity then how scientists could guess about the gravitational force.

## How can you say that gravitational force is a field force?

(MUN. GII, 2016) (SGD. GI, 2019) (MLM. GI, 1022)
Ans. Gravitational force is a non-contact force. For example, the velocity of a body, thrown up, goes on decreasing while on retum its velocity goes on increasing. This is due to the gravitational pull of the Earth acting on the body whether the body is in contact with the Earth or not. Such a force is called the field force. It is assumed that a gravitational field exists all around the Earth and its direction is towards the centre of the Earth. The gravitational field becomes weaker and weaker as we go farther and farther away from the Earth.
5.7. Explain, what is meant by gravitational field strength?
(RWP. GII, 2014)

> (SWL GI, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI \& GI, 2015) (GRW. GI, SWL. GI, SGD. GI, 2016) (FSD. GI, MLN. GI, SGD. GI, 2017)
> (IHR. GII, MLM. GI, SGD. GI, 2018)/MUM. GI, RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2019)(SWL. GI, 2021) (LHR. GI, MLM. GI, BWP. GI, 2022)
> (FSD. GI \& GI, MLM. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2023)

Ans. The gravitational field becomes weaker and weaker as we go farther and farther away from the Earth. In the gravitational field of the Earth, the gravitational force per unit mass is called the gravitational field strength of the Earth. At any place its value is equal to the value of $g$ at that point. Near the surface of the Earth, the gravitational field strength is $10 \mathrm{Nkg}^{-1}$.

## Why is law of gravitation important to us? <br> (FSD. GI, MLM. G. 2014) (DGK. GII. 2016) (SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)

Newton's law of gravitation is very important to us. Because life can not imagine without this. This is the force of gravitation which is responsible for the survival of every object in the universe. We can determine the mass of Earth, density of Earth and orbital speed of satellite only because of this law. Artificial satellites are used for communication purposes, and carry instruments or passengers to perform experiments in space. These satellites require centripetal force that keeps them to move around the Earth. The gravitation force of attraction between the satellite and the Earth provides the necessary centripetal force.

### 5.111:

## How can the mass of Earth be determined? (Subjective Type Question)

(LHR. GI, RWP. GI \& GI, DGK. GI, MLN. GI \& GI, BWP. GI, SGD. GI, 2015) (MLM. GI, BWP. GI \& GI, 2021)
(GRW. GI, MLN. GI, SWL. GI, SGD. GI, BWP. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2023)
Ans. For answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
5.11: Can you determine the mass of our moon? If yes, then what you do need to know?

Ans. Yes, we can find out the mass of moon by using the law of gravitation.
As we know.

$$
M=\frac{R^{2} g}{G}
$$

To find out the value of mass of moon, we need to know, following factors.
Radius of the moon (R)
Gravitational acceleration of the moon (g)
Gravitational constant (G).

### 5.12 :

## Why does the value of $\mathbf{g}$ vary from place to place?

(SGD. GI, 2014) (SWL. GI, SGD. GII, BWP. GII, 2015) (LHR. GII, FSD. GII, 2016)
(FSD. GII, MLN. GI \& GI, SWL GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2017) (MLN. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2018)

(FSD. GI, MLN. GI, SWL GI, DGK. GI \& GII, 2019) (SWL. GII, SGD. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, SWL. GI, BWP. GI, 2023)

Ans. As we know that the value of gravitational acceleration depends on the radius of the Earth.

$$
g=\frac{G M_{e}}{R^{2}}
$$

Value of (g) is inversely proportional to the radius of Earth. This varies with height. By increasing height the value of $g$ will decrease and by decreasing height the value of $g$ will increase. This is the reason that the value of $g$ is greater at sea level than at the hills.

### 5.13: Explain how the value of g varies with altitude. <br> (DGK. GII, 2015) (SWL GI, RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2016) (SWL. GII, 2017) (GRW. GI, 2018) <br> (RWP. GI, BWP. GII, 2019) (LHR. GI, 2022)

Ans. -As we know $\mathrm{g}=\frac{\mathrm{GM}_{\mathrm{e}}}{\mathrm{R}^{2}}$ This equation shows that the value of acceleration due to gravity g depends on the radius of the Earth at its surface. The value of $g$ is inversely proportional to the square of the radius of the Earth. But it does not remain constant. It decreases with altitude. Altitude is the height of the body or place from the sea level. The value of $g$ is greater at sea level than at the hills. Consider a body of mass ( m ) at an altitude ( h ). The distance of the body from the centre of the Earth becomes R+h.

$$
g_{h}=G \frac{M_{e}}{(R+h)^{2}}
$$

According to this equation, we come to know that at a height equal to one Earth radius above the surface of the Earth, $g$ becomes one fourth of its value on the Earth. Similarly at a distance of two Earth's radius above the Earth's surface, the value of $g$ becomes one ninth of its value on the Earth.

### 5.14: What are artificial satellites?

(FSD. GI, SWL. GI, 2014)(FSD. GI, DGK. GI, 2019)
(SWL GI, GRW. GI, SGD. GII, DGK GI, BWP. GII, 2016) (GRW. GII, SWL GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GI, 2018)
(SWL GII, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI \& GII, SWL GI, 2021)
(SWL GI \& GI, DGK. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, FSD, GII, SWL GI, BWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2023)
Ans. Scientists have sent many objects into space. Some of these objects revolve around the Earth. These are called artificial satellites.
5.15: How Newton's law of gravitation helps in understanding the motion of satellites?

Ans. A satellite requires centripetal force that keeps it to move around the Earth The gravitational force of attraction between the satellite and the Earth provides the necessary centripetal force. This centripetal force is introduced by the Newton. So in this way Newton's law of gravitation helps in understanding the motion of satellites.

### 5.16: On what factors the orbital speed of a satellite depends?

(BWP. GI, 2014) (RWP. GII, SGD. GI, 2015) (LHR. GII, 2016) (MLN. GII, RWP. GII, BWP. GI, 2017) (SWL. GII, 2019) (GRW. GI, FSD. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GII, 2021) (GRW. GI, SWL GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, 2022) (MLN. GI, 2023)
Ans. Orbital speed of the satellite depends only on gravitational acceleration of Earth and radius of the Earth. It is clear from the given formula. $\mathrm{v}_{\mathrm{o}}=\sqrt{\mathrm{gR}}$

### 5.17: Why communication satellites are stationed at geostationary orbits?

(GRW. GI, DGK. GI, SWL GII, 2014)(SWL GII, 2015) (GRW. GII, MLN. GII, SWL GI, 2016)
(GRW. GII, 2017) (SWL. GII, 2019) (GRW. GI, 2022)
Ans. Geostationary satellites take 24 hours to complete their one revolution around the Earth. As Earth also completes its one rotation about its axis in 24 hours, hence, these geostationary satellites appear to be stationary with respect to Earth.

1. The idea of gravity was put up first by:
   (RWP. GI, 2014) (SGD. GII, 2018)

   (B) Newton
   (C) Hook
   (D) Einstein
2. According to the law of gravitation ' $F$ ' is equal to: (GRW. GII, 2016)(BWP. GII, 2017) (MLN. GI, 2022) (GRW. GII, 2023)
   (A) $G \frac{m_{1} m_{2}}{d^{5}}$
   (B) $G \frac{m_{1} m_{2}}{d^{4}}$
   (C) $G \frac{m_{1} m_{2}}{d^{3}}$
   (D) $\mathrm{G} \frac{\mathrm{m}_{1} \mathrm{~m}_{2}}{\mathrm{~d}^{2}}$

## $\mathbf{6 . 1}+\mathbf{6 . 2}+\mathbf{6 . 3}$ Work + Energy + Kinetic Energy

1. The product of force and displacement is called:
   (DGK GL, 2022)
   (A) Acceleration
   (B) Momentum
   (C) Power
   (D) Work
2. One ioule is equal to:
   (SWL, GII, 2014)(RWP. GI, 2019)
   (A) $\frac{1 \mathrm{~N}}{\mathrm{Im}}$
   (B) $1 \mathrm{~N} \times 1 \mathrm{~m}$
   (C) $\frac{1 \mathrm{~m}}{1 \mathrm{~N}}$
   (D) $\frac{1 \mathrm{~N}^{2}}{1 \mathrm{~m}^{2}}$
   (DGK. Gl, 2018)
3. The formula of kinetic energy is:
   (C) $\frac{1}{2} m v^{2}$
   (D) mv
   (A) $\mathrm{mv}^{2} / \mathrm{r}$
   (B) mgh
4. If the velocity of a body becomes three times greater then Kinetic energy will be:
   (A) Nine times
   (B) Three times
   (C) Four times
   (C) Four times
   (D) Six times
   (GRW. GII, 2022)

Answers

1. Work
2. $1 \mathrm{~N} \times 1 \mathrm{~m}$
3. $\frac{1}{2} \mathrm{mv}^{2}$
4. Nine times
5. Nine times

## Short Questions developed according to the New Examination Techniques

## (Knowledge, Understanding, Application, Analytical and Conceptual) of the Education Department.

## $6.3+6.4+6.5$ Kinetic Energy + Potential Energy + Forms of Energy

1. Define work and its S.I. Unit.
   (BWP. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Work: Work is said to be done when a force acting on a body displaces in the direction of the force.
   Unit: SI unit of work is Joule.
2.

Define potential energy and write its equation.
(DGK. GI, 2017) (DGK. GI, 2017) (RWP. GI, DGK. GII, 2018)
(LHR. GI, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, SWL. GII, BWP. GI, 2019) (RWP. GII, 2021) (SWL GII, 2022) (FSD. GII, DGK. GII, 2023)
Ans. The ability of a body to do work due to its position is known as its potential energy or gravitational potential energy.
Equation: P.E = mgh 3. What is the difference between work and energy?
(GRW. GII, MLN. GII, 2016) (SWL. GII, 2019) (SWL. GI, 2022)
Ans. Work: In physics, work is said to be done when a force acts on a body and moves it in the direction of force.
Energy: The ability of a body to do wok is called energy. 4. Differentiate between mechanical and chemical energy.
(SGD. GI, 2014) (LHR. GI, SWL. GI, 2016) (MLN. GI, 2022)
Ans. Mechanical energy: The energy possessed by a body both due to its motion or position is called mechanical energy.
Examples: Water running down a stream, wind, a moving car, a lifted hammer, a stretched bow, a catapult or a compressed spring etc. possess mechanical energy.
Chemical Energy: Chemical energy is present in food, fuels and in other substances. The energy is released from these substances during chemical reactions. 5. Differentiate between Potential energy and Kinetic energy.
(DGK GI, 2022) (SGD. GI, 2023)
Ans.

| Potential energy                                                                            | Kinetic energy                                                                      |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | :---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The ability of a body to do work due to its <br> position is known as its potential energy. | The energy possessed by a body due to its <br> motion is called its kinetic energy. |

## 6. Define fission reaction.

(DGK GII, 2017)
Ans. In fission reaction, the heavy nucleus of an atom splits up into smaller parts releasing a large amount of energy. Nuclear power plants give out a lot of nuclear reactions and vast amount of heat. 7. Write two process for the emission of nuclear energy.
(BWP. GII, 2017)
Ans. 1. Fission Reaction 2. Fusion Reaction 8. Define heat energy? Write its some sources?

Ans. Heat energy: Heat is a form of energy given out by hot bodies.

## Sources of heat energy:

⇒ Large amount of heat is obtained by burning fuel.
⇒ Heat is produced when motion is opposed by frictional forces.
⇒ The Sun is the main source of heat energy.
The foods which are eaten by humans provide heat energy to them.

1. What is the second name of solar cell and how it is made? (FSD. GI. 2016)(RWP. GII, 2018)(LHR. GII, 2019)

Ans. Solar energy can be converted directly into electricity by solar cells. A solar cell also called photocell is made from silicon wafer. 2. By defining magma, describe geothermal energy. (FSD. GII, 2014)(RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2016)(GRW. GII, 2017)

Ans. There is hot molten part, deep in the Earth called magma. Water reaching close to the magma changes to steam due to the high temperature of magma. This energy is called geothermal energy. 3. What is Bio mass and how energy is produced from it?
(RWP. G. 2014) (GRW. GII, DGK. GI, 2015) (GRW. GI \& GI, 2017 ) (MLN. GI, FSD. GII, DGK. GII, 2018)
Ans. Biomas: Biomass is plant or animal wastes that can be burnt as fuel.
When animal dung, dead plants and dead animals decompose, they give off a mixture of methate and carbon dioxide which is used to generate electricity. 4. Differentiate between sound energy and light energy.

Ans. Sound energy: Sound is a form of energy. Sound is produced when a body vibrates.
(DGK. Gl, 2023)
Light energy: Light energy can be obtained from candles, electric bulbs, fluorescent tubes and also by burning fuel. Sun is the great source of light energy. 5. What is meant by Biomass energy?
(DGK. GI, 2015) (MLN. GII, 2023)
Ans. Biomass energy: Biomass is plant or animal wastes that can be burnt a fuel. Other forms of biomass are garbage, farm wastes, sugarcane and other plants. 6. What is meant by non-renewable source? Write an example.
(DGK. GII, 2015) (BWP. GII, 2017)
Ans. Non-renewable source: The fossile fuels took millions of years for their formation, so, they are known as non-renewable resources.
For example: Oil, gas, coal. 7. Write two disadvantages of Fossil Fuels.
(BWP. GI, 2015) (LHR. GII, 2017) (LHR. GII, BWP. GI, 2018) (FSD. GI, 2022)
Ans. ⇒ Once the supply of fossil fuels is exhausted, the world would face serious energy crisis.
⇒ Fossil fuels would not be able to meet our future energy demands.
⇒ Exhausted supply of fossil fuels would cause serious social and economical problems for countries like us. 8. Write the names of the parts of Solar Heating System. (DGK. GI. RWP. GII. 2016)(MLN. GII, 2017)(RWP. GII. 2019)

Ans. A heating system consists of
is A collecter is A storage device is A distribution system 9. What is meant by fossil fuels?

Ans. Fossil fuels are usually hydrocarbons (compounds of carbon and hydrogen). When they are burnt, they combine with oxygen from the air. The carbon becomes carbon dioxide, hydrogen becomes hydrogen oxide called water, while energy is released as heat. 10. Define geothermal energy and elastic potential energy.
(GRW. GII, 2018)
Ans. There is hot molten part, deep in the Earth called magma. Water reaching close to the magma changes to steam due to the high temperature of magma. This energy is called geothermal energy. 11. What is meant by geothermal energy?
(FSD. GI, 2018)
Ans. There is hot molten part, deep in the Earth called magma. Water reaching close to the magma changes to steam due to the high temperature of magma. This energy is called geothermal energy. 12. Differentiate between solar cell and solar panels.
(GRW. GI. 2019)(MLN. GI, 2023)
Ans. Difference between solar cell and solar panels:

| Solar Cells                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Solar Panels                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Solar energy can also be converted directly into <br> electricity by solar cells. A solar cells also called photot <br> cell is made from silicon wafer. When sunlight falls on a <br> solar cell, it converts the light directly into electrical <br> energy. Solar cells are used in calculators, watches and <br> toys. | Large numbers of solar cells are wired <br> together to form solar panels. Solar panels <br> can provide power to telephone booths, light <br> houses and scientific research centres. Solar <br> panels are also used to power satellites. |

## 13. How do we gain energy from air?

(SWL GI, 2019)
Ans. Wind has been used as a source of energy for centuries. It has powered sailing ships across the sea.
It has been used by windmills to grind grass and pump water. 14. Write down two causes of thermal pollution.

Ans. 1. Natural processes such as volcanic eruptions, forest fires and dust storms add pollutants to the air.
These pollutant, rarely build up to harmful levels and are very dangerous for health. 2. The burning of fuel and solid wastes in homes, automobiles and factories releases harmful
amount of air pollutant. 15. What is meant by nuclear fuels?

Ans. Nuclear Fuels: In nuclear power plants, the fuel use for fission reaction is called nuclear fuels. 16. What is meant by Solar House Heating?
(GRW. GI, 1022)
Ans. Solar House Heating: A solar house heating is use solar energy to heat a water and then transfer the solar heat directly to the interior space for later use.
Solar house heating system consists on the following parts:
Collector, storage device and distribution system. 17. Define magma.
(SGD. GI, RWP. GII, DGK. GI, 2012) (SWL. GI \& GII, 2023)
Ans. Magma: There is hot molten part, deep in the Earth called magma. Water reaching close to the magma changes to steam due to the high temperature of magma. 18. How Solar Panels are formed? Write down their uses.
(BWP. GI, 2022) (FSD. GI, 2023)
Ans. Solar Panels: Large numbers of solar cells are wired together to form solar panels. Solar panels can provide power to telephone booths, light houses and scientific research centres. Solar panels are also used to power satellites. 19. What is a solar cell? Write down its uses.
(LHR. GI, 2023)
Ans. Solar Cells: Solar energy can also be converted directly into electricity by solar cells.
Solar cells is also called photo cell.
Uses of solar cells: Solar cells can provide power to telephone booths, light houses and scientific research centres.
⇒ Solar cells are also used to power satellites. 20. How does energy produce by burning fossil fuels?
(MLN. GII, 2023)
Ans. Fossil fuels are usually hydrocarbons (compounds of carbon and hydrogen). When they are burnt, they combine with oxygen from the air. The carbon becomes carbon dioxide, hydrogen becomes hydrogen oxide called water, while energy is released as heat. 21. Define wind energy.
(SWL GI, 2023)
Ans. Wind energy describes the process by which the wind is used to generate mechanical power or electricity.
Wind turbines convert the kinetic energy in the wind into mechanical power.

## $6.8+6.9$ Etficiency + Power

1. A cyclist does 12 J of useful work while pedalling, his bike from energy 100 joules of food energy which he takes. What is his efficiency?
   (DGK GI, 2014) (SGD. GI, 2021)
   Sol. Useful work done by the cyclist $=12 \mathrm{~J}$
   Energy used by the cyclist $=100 \mathrm{~J}$

$$
\begin{aligned}
\text { Efficiency } & =\frac{12 \mathrm{~J}}{100 \mathrm{~J}}=0.12 \\
\text { or \% efficiency } & =0.12 \times 100=12 \%
\end{aligned}
$$

The efficiency of the cyclist is $12 \%$. 2. Define efficiency and write its equation in percentage.
(FSD. GI, MLN. GI, SWL. GI, 2017)
(LHR. GII, GRW. GI, MLN. GII. SGD. GII, BWP. GII, 2018) (SGD. GI, BWP. GII, 2019)
(FSD. GI, SWL GII, MLN. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GII, 2021) (RWP. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GII, 2023)
Ans. Efficiency of a system is the ratio of required form of enregy obtained from a system as output to the total energy given to it as input.

$$
\begin{aligned}
& \text { i.e. efficiency }=\frac{\text { required form of output }}{\text { Total input energy }} \\
& \% \text { efficiency }=\frac{\text { required form of output }}{\text { Total input energy }} \times 100
\end{aligned}
$$

3. Define watt and write how much watt is equal to one horsepower?
   (SWL GII, SGD. GII, 2014)(FSD. GI, 2015) (MLN. GII, BWP. GII, 2019) (SGD. GII, 2021) (RWP. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, RWP. GI, BWP. G. 2023)
   Ans. Watt: The power of a body is one watt if it does work at the rate of 1 joule per second ( $1 \mathrm{Js}^{-1}$ ) 1 horse power $=1 \mathrm{hp}=746$ watt
4. Define joule and watt.

Ans. SI unit of work is joule (J).
(GRW. Gl. 2018)
Joule: The amount of work is one joule when a force of one Newton displaces a body through one metre in the direction of force.
Thus, $1 \mathrm{~J}=1 \mathrm{~N} \times 1 \mathrm{~m}$
Watt:The SI unit of power is watt as:
The power of a body is one watt if it does work at the rate of 1 joule per second ( $1 \mathrm{Js}-1$ ). 5. If a pump has power of 1120 watt. Convert it into horse power (hp).
(DGK. Gl, 2019) (DGK. Gl, 2021)

| Sol.Power $=\mathrm{P}$ | $=1120 \mathrm{watt}$               |
| ----------------------: | :---------------------------------- |
|                 As 1 hp | $=746 \mathrm{watt}$                |
|             or 746 watt | $=1 \mathrm{hp}$                    |
|                     1 W | $=\frac{1}{746} \mathrm{hp}$        |
|                   Power | $=\mathrm{P}=1120 \mathrm{~W}$      |
|                         | $=\frac{1120}{746}=1.5 \mathrm{hp}$ |

6. Define efficiency and power. (FSD. GII, 2022)

Ans. Efficiency: A body possesses energy if it is capable to do work.
Efficiency $=\frac{\text { required form of output }}{\text { Total input energy }}$
Power: Power is defined as the rate of doing work.
Power $=\frac{\text { work done }}{\text { time taken }}$

$$
P=\frac{W}{t}
$$

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

6.2: Define work. What is its SI unit? (MLn. GII, DGK. GII, SGD. GII, 2014)(LHR. GI8I, FSD. GII, MLN. GI, RWP. GI, 2015) (SWL. GII, 2016) (GRW. GII, MLN. GI, 2017) (DGK. GII, 202I) (LHR. GI, MLN. GII, SWL. GII, DGK. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, FSD, GI, SWL. GI, BWP. GI, 2023)
Ans. Work: Work is said to be done when a force acting on a body displaces it in the direction of the force.
Work $=$ Force × distance
SI unit of work: SI unit of work is joule (J)
Definition of joule: The amount of work is one joule when a force of one newton displaces a body through one metre in the direction of force.
6.3. When does a force do work? Explain.
(SGD. GII, 2015)
Ans. When a force acting on a body displaces it through some distance S in the direction of force as shown in the given figure, it does work on a body.

![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/21d4fa44-98b0-4da0-9d17-ba9c24136ff3-47.jpg?height=182&width=657&top_left_y=1111&top_left_x=808)
Work done in displacing a body in the direction of force

Sometimes the force and displacement do not have the same direction such as shown in figure.
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/21d4fa44-98b0-4da0-9d17-ba9c24136ff3-47.jpg?height=236&width=679&top_left_y=1333&top_left_x=800)

In this case, force $\mathbf{F}$ is making an angle ( $\theta$ ) with the surface on which body is moved. Resolving $\mathbf{F}$ into its perpendicular components $\mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{x}}$ and $\mathrm{F}_{\mathrm{y}}$ as;

$$
\begin{aligned}
& F_{x}=F \cos \theta \\
& F_{y}=F \sin \theta
\end{aligned}
$$

In case when force and displacement are not parallel then only the $\mathbf{x}$-component $\mathbf{F}_{\mathbf{x}}$ parallel to the surface causes the body to move on the surface and the $y$-component Fy .
Hence

$$
\begin{aligned}
& W=F \times S \\
& W=(F \cos \theta) S=F S \cos \theta
\end{aligned}
$$

6.4: Why do we need energy?
(DGK. GII, 2016) (SWL. GII, BWP. GII, 2022)

Energy is necessary for running and walking for humans.
6.5: Define energy, give two types of mechanical energy. (MLN. GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (GRW. GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2021)

Ans. Energy: A body possesses energy if it is capable to do work.
Types of mechanical energy: Mechanical energy has two following types.
(i) Kinetic energy.
(ii) Potential energy.

6.13: What is meant by the efficiency of a system?
(RWP. GII, BWP. GI, MLN. GI \& GII, GRW. GII, 2015)
(SWL GI, GRW. GII, SGD. GI, 2016) (LHR. GI \& GII, GRW. GII, SWL GI, BWP. GI \& GII, 2021) (FSD. GI, 2022) (BWP. GII, 2023]

6.14: How can you find the efficiency of a system?
(DGK. GII, MLN. GII, 2022)
Ans. Efficiency of a system can be found out by following formula.

$$
\begin{aligned}
& \text { Efficiency }=\frac{\text { required form of output }}{\text { totalinput energy }} \\
& \% \text { Efficiency }=\frac{\text { required form of output }}{\text { total input energy }} \times 100
\end{aligned}
$$

6.15. What is meant by the term power?
(LHR. GII, SWL GI, FSD. GI, RWP. GI \& GII, SGD. GI, 2014)
(LHR. GII, MLN. GI \& GII, GRW. GI, DGK. GI, FSD. GII, SWL. GI, SGD. GI, 2015) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, 2016) (LHR. GI, SWL GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, 2017)
(LHR. GI, GRW. GII, MLN. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2018) (LHR. GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2019) (SWL. GI, SGD. GI, 2012)
(LHR. GI, GRW. GI, FSD. GI \& GII, SWL. GI \& GII, MLN. GI \& GII, DGK, GII, BWP. GI, 2021) (SWL. GI, SGD. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, FSD. GII, 2023)
Ans. Power is defined as the rate of doing work.
Power $=\frac{\text { work done }}{\text { time taken }} \quad \Rightarrow \quad \mathrm{P}=\frac{\mathrm{W}}{\mathrm{t}}$
The unit of power is watt. Bigger units of power are kilowatt (kW), megawatt (MW) etc.
6.16: Define watt.
(GRW. GI, 2014) (LHR, GI, MLN. GI, SGD. GII, DGK GI, 2016)
(GRW. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2017) (DGK. GII, BWP. GI, 2018) (FSD. GII, 2019) (BWP. GII, 107)
Ans. The power of a body is one watt if it does work at the rate of 1 joule per second (1Js-1).

## 7.2 + 7.6 Density + Archimedes Principle

   (C) Three
   (D) Four

   (DGK Gil, 2019)

   (B) $100 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
   (C) $10 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$

   (B) 1.1
   (C) 1.2
   (D) 1.3

   (LHR. GII, 2022)
   (A) $D=\frac{w_{2}}{w_{1}-w_{2}} \times p$
   (B) $D=\frac{w_{1}}{w_{1}-w_{2}} \times \rho$
   (C) $D=\frac{w_{1}-w_{2}}{w_{1}} \times \rho$
   (D) $D=\frac{w_{1}}{w_{2}-w_{1}} \times \rho$

## Answers

1. 13.6
2. Three
3. $1000 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
4.

1.35.
$\mathrm{D}=\frac{\mathrm{w}_{1}}{\mathrm{w}_{1}-\mathrm{w}_{2}} \times \rho$

Q. 1 Encircle the correct answer from the given choices.
i. In which of the following state molecules do not leave their position?
(LHR. GII, 2015) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI, SGD. GII, 2016) (GRW. GI, MLN. GII, SWL. GI \& GII, DGK. GI, 2017) (GRW. GII, SWL. GII, 2018) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI \& GII, MLN. GI, 2021) (LHR. GI, SWL. GII, 2022) (SWL. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI \& GI, 2023)

(b) liquid
(c) gas
(d) plasma

Which of the substances is the lightest one?
(SWL GI, DGK, GI, RWP. GI \& GI, 2014)
(LHR. GII, SWL GI, 2015) (LHR. GII, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, DGK GI, BWP. GI, 2016) (LHR. GI, 2017)

## Short Questions developed according to the New Examination Techniques (Knowledge, Understanding, Application, Analytical and Conceptual) of the Education Department.

![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/4f2fad85-1ae9-4174-b5eb-39803a2d3260-52.jpg?height=147&width=1199&top_left_y=1832&top_left_x=210)

1.

Write some important features of kinetic molecular model of matter.
(LHR. GI, MLN. GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GI \& GII, BWP. GI, 2014) (GRW. GI, FSD. GII, SWL, GII, DGK, GI, 2015) (LHR.GI, GRW. GI, RWP. GI, 2016)
Ans. Kinetic theory has some important features.
(MLN. GI, FSD. GII, SWL GII, BWP. GI, 2017) (GRW. GII, MLN. GI, SGD. GI, 2018) (SGD. GII, 2019) (SGD. GII, 2022) (SGD. GI, 2023)

- Matter is made up of particles called molecules.
- The molecules remain in continuous motion.
- Molecules attract each other.

2. Write one difference and one similarity between ships and submarines?

Ans. > Ships and boats are designed on the principle of floatation. They carry passengers and goods over water.

- A submarine can travel over as well as under water. It also works on the principle of floatation. What is the difference between Stress and Strain?

Ans. Stress: Stress is defined as the force acting on unit area at the surface of a body. Stress is related to the force producing deformation.
Strain: When stress acts on a body, it may change its length, volume, or shape. A comparison of such a change caused by the stress with the orignal length, volume or shape is called as starin.

What is barometer and define strain.
(DGK. GII, 2018)
Ans. Barometer: The instrument that measure atmospheric pressure is called barometer.
Strain: When stress acts on a body, it may change its length, volume, or shape. A comparison of such a change caused by the stress with the original length, volume or shape is called as starin. 5. Write down the formula of pressure and strain.
(LHR. GI, 2021)
Ans. Pressure $=\frac{\text { Force }}{\text { Area }}$

$$
\mathrm{P}=\frac{\mathrm{F}}{\mathrm{~A}}
$$

And

$$
\text { Strain }=\frac{\text { Change in shape }}{\text { Original shape }}
$$

6. Define density and elasticity.

$$
\rho=\frac{m}{V}\left(\operatorname{lgm}^{-3}\right)
$$

(GRW. GII, BWP. GI, 2021)

Ans. Density: Density of a substance is defined as its mass per unit volume.
Elasticity: The property of a body to restore its original size and shape as the deforming force ceases to act is called elasticity. 7. Define elasticity and stress.
(LHR. GII, 2019) (DGK. GI, 2022)
Ans. Elasticity: The property of a body to restore its original size and shape as the deforming force ceases to act is called elasticity.
Stress: The force acting on unit area at the surface of a body is called stress.

$$
\text { Stress }=\frac{\text { Force }}{\text { Area }}
$$

8. Define Hooke's Law and write its equation.
   (SGD. GI, MLN. GII, 2015) (GRW.GII.RWP.GII. DGK. GI \& GI, 2016)
   (LHR. GI, GRW. GI \& GII, MLN. GI, BWP. GII, 2017) (GRW. GI, FSD. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI \& GI, 2021)
   (LHR. GI, FSD. GI, SWL GII, 2022) (FSD. GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GII, 2023)
   Ans. Hooke's law: The strain produced in a body by the stress applied to it is directly proportional to the stress within the elastic limit of the body is called Hooke's law.
   ![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/4f2fad85-1ae9-4174-b5eb-39803a2d3260-53.jpg?height=85&width=226&top_left_y=1816&top_left_x=644)

Equation: $\frac{\text { Stress }}{\text { Strain }}=$ Constant

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

2. How is kinetic molecular model of matter helpful in differentiating various states of matter?
   Ans. Kinetic molecular model of matter explains the three states of matter solids, liquids and gases.
   According to kinetic molecular model of matter,
   The molecules of solids are held closed together. Solid have fixed shapes and volumes.
   In liquids the distance between the molecules is more than in solids. Liquids have fixed volumes but they attain the shape of a container in which they are put. Gases have no fixed shape or volume. Their molecules are much apart from each other.
   7.3. Does there exist a fourth state of matter? What is that?

Ans. Yes, there exist a fourth state of matter that is called plasma.
At very high temperature, the matter assumes the state of ions and electrons this is called plasma.
7.4: What is meant by density? What is its SI unit?
(LHR. GII, SWL GI, 2017) (GRW.GI,MLN. GI, SWL. GI, RWP. GI, 2018) (GRW. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GII, BWP. GII, 2019)
(LHR. GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, SWL GI, DGK. GI \& GII, BWP. GII, RWP. GI, 2021) (MLN. GI, 2022)
(LHR. GI \& GII, MLN. GI, SWL GII, RWP. GI, 2023)
Ans. Density of a substance is defined as the mass per unit volume.

$$
\begin{aligned}
\text { density } & =\frac{\text { mass }}{\text { volume }} \\
d & =\frac{m}{V}
\end{aligned}
$$

The SI unit of dens kilogramme per cubic metre ( $\mathrm{kg} \mathrm{m}^{-3}$ ).

## Can we use a hydrometer to measure the density of milk?

(GRW. GI, 2014)
Ans. Hydrometer is a device which is used to measure the density of fluid. As the hydrometer is a glass tube with a scale marked on its stem and heavy weight in the bottom. It is partially immersed in the milk that is also a fluid, the density of which is to be measured, hence we can use hydrometer to measure the density of milk.

## 7.6: Define the term pressure.

(GRW. GI, FSD. GI, RWP. GI, SGD. GI \& GII, BWP. GI, 2014)

> (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, FSD. GI, 2015) (LHR.GI \& GII, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2016) (RWP. GI, MLN. GI, SWL GI, SGD. GI, 2017)
> (FSD. GI, LHR. GI, SWL GII, BWP. GI \& GI, 2018) (FSD. GI \& GII, MLN. GII, DGK. GI, BWP. GII, 2019)
> (FSD. GI \& GII, SWL GII, MLN. GI, SGD. GII, RWP. GII, 2021) (LHR. GI, FSD. GII, SGD. GI \& GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)

(GRW. GI, MLN. GI, RWP. GII, 2023)
Ans. The force acting normally on unit area at the surface of a body is called pressure.

$$
\begin{aligned}
\text { Pressure } & =\frac{\text { force }}{\text { area }} \\
P & =\frac{F}{A}
\end{aligned}
$$

In SI, the unit of pressure is newton per square metre $\left(\mathrm{Nm}^{-2}\right)$.

## 7.7: Show that atmosphere exerts pressure. (Subjective Type Question)

Ans. For answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
7.8. It is easy to remove air from a balloon but it is very difficult to remove air from a glass bottle. Why?
Ans. It is very difficult to remove air from a glass bottle because air pressure in the bottle is less than atmospheric pressure.
7.9: What is a barometer? (SWL GI, DGK. GII, 2014) (FSD. GI, DGK. GI \& GII, 2016) (DGK. GII, 2017) (LHR. GI, 2018) (FSD. GI, MLN. GII, 2022)

Ans. The instrument that measures atmospheric pressure is called barometer. One of the simple barometer is mercury barometer. Atmospheric pressure at sea level is 101300 pa.

### 7.10: Why is water not suitable to be used in a barometer?

(LHR GII, 2014)(RWP. GI, 2017) (SGD. GII, 2018) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI, RWP. GI, 2021)
Ans. As we know that mercury is 13.6 times more dense than water, Atmospheric pressure can hold vertical column of water about 13.6 times greater than the height of mercury column at that place. Thus, at sea level vertical height of water column would be $0.76 \mathrm{~m} \times 13.6=10.34 \mathrm{~m}$. Thus, we would need a glass tube more than 10 m long or approximately 11 m to make a water barometer that is too long, therefore water is not suitable to be used in barometer.

### 7.11: What makes a sucker pressed on a smooth wall sticks to it?

Ans. A wall sucker sticks to wall because of the difference in pressure between wall and rubber sucker
which causes adhesion. This sucker sticks on the smooth wall or in other words the pressure on the outside becomes greater than the pressure on the inside.

## nib

![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/4f2fad85-1ae9-4174-b5eb-39803a2d3260-55.jpg?height=255&width=224&top_left_y=210&top_left_x=642)

### 7.12. Why does the atmospheric pressure vary with height?

(DGK. GI, 2018) (GRW. GII, RWP. GI, 2019) (GRW. GII, DGK GI, 2021) (LHR GI \& GI, BWP. GII, 2022)

Ans. As we know Earth's atmosphere extends upward about a few hundred kilometres with continuously decreasing density, and the pressure is directly proportional to the density, therefore as we going up, the atmospheric air becomes thinner and thinner, so, density also reduces. Even at a height of about 30 km , the atmospheric pressure becomes only 7 mm of Hg , (mercury) which is approximately 1000 Pa . It would become zero at an altitude where there is no air.

### 7.13: What does it mean when the atmospheric pressure at a place fall suddenly?

(GRW. GII, 2016) (MLN. GI, 2018)
Ans. A sudden fall in atmospheric pressure often followed by a storm, rain and typhoon to occur in few hours time.

### 7.14: What changes are expected in weather if the barometer reading shows a sudden increase?

(SGD. GI, 2014)
Ans. If the barometer reading shows a sudden increase, or a rapid increase in atmospheric pressure, means that it will soon be followed by a decrease in the atmospheric pressure indicating poor weather ahead.

### 7.15: State Pascal's law.

(GRW. GI \& GII, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2018) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, BWP. GII, 2019)
(GRW. GI, FSD. GII, 2022) (LHR. GII, FSD. GII, MLM. GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2023)
Ans. Pressure applied at any point of a liquid enclosed in a container, is transmitted without loss to all other parts of liquid.
7.16: Explain the working of hydraulic press. (Subjactive Type Question)

Ans. For answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
7.17: What is meant by elasticity?
(MLN. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI. BWP. GII, 2014) (SGD. GI, 2015)
(LHR. GII, SWL GI, SGD. GI, 2016) (LHR. GI \& GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2017) (LHR. GIT, RWP. GI, BWP. GL, 2018) (FSD. GII, 2019) (LHR. GII, FSD. GII, SWL GI, DGK. GI, 2021) (GRW. GII, MLN. GI, SWL, GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)
(GRW. GI \& GII, FSD. GII, MLN. GII, 2023)
Ans. Easticity is the property of matter by virtue of which matter resists any force which tries to change its length, shape or volume.

### 7.18: State Archimedes principle.

(FSD. GII, SWL GII, 2014) (SGD. GII, 2015) (LHR. GII, MLN. GII, SWL. GI \& GII, SGD. GI, 2016)<br>(LHR. GII, RWP. GI \& GII, 2018) (LHR. GII, MLN. GI \& GII, SGD. GI, RWP. GII, SGD. GI, 2019) (SGD. GI, 2022)<br>(GRW. GI, FSD. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GI, 2023)

Ans. When an object is wholly or partially immersed in a liquid, it loses its weight equal to the weight of the liquid displaced. This is known as Archimedes principle.
7.19: What is upthrust? Explain the principle of floatation. (GRW. GII, DGK, GI, 2017)(DGK, GI \& GI, 2019)(RWP. G. 2022)

Ans. Upthrust: Upthrust is an upward force which acts on an object kept inside a liquid. It apparently makes the object to lose weight.

## Principle of floatation: For answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".

### 7.20: Explain how a submarine floats the water surface and dives down into water.

(FSD. GI, 2014) (MLN. GII, 2018) (GRW. GII, 2019)
Ans. A submarine can travel over as well as under water. It works on the principle of floatation. It has a system of tanks which can be filled with and emptied from seawater. Submarine floats over water
when the weight of the water equal to its volume is greater than its weight Under this condition, it is similar to a ship and remains partially above water level.
⇒ When the tanks of submarine are filled, the weight of the submarine increases. As soon as its weight becomes greater than the upthrust, it dives into water and remains underwater.

### 7.21: W

Why does a piece of stone sink in water but a ship with a huge weight floats?
(LHR. GII, 2014) (LHR. GII, 2015) (MLN. GII, 2016) (BWP. GI, 2019) (MLN. GII, RWP. GI, 2027)
Ans. Ships and boats float on water. It is becausse the weight of an equal volume of water is greater than the weight of ships and boats.
A stone sinks in water. It is because the weight of an equal volume of water is smaller than the weight of stone.
7.22: What is Hooke's law? What is meant by elastic limit?
(MLN. GII, SWL GI \& GII, SGD. GI, DGK, GI \& GII, 2018)
(LHR. GI, GRW. GII, FSD. GII, SWL GI \& GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, MLN. GII, BWP. GII, 202I’
Ans. Hooke's law: The strain produced in a body by the stress applied to it is directly proportional to the stress within the elastic limit of the body is called Hooke's law.
stress $\propto$ strain
Elastic limit: Elastic limit can be defined as a limit within which a body recovers its original length, volume or shape after the deforming force is removed.
7.23. Take a rubber band. Construct a balance of your own using a rubber band. Check its accuracy by weighing various objects.
Ans. I took a rubber band. And constructed a balance of mine using a rubber band. Then i measured the weight of various objects to check its accuracy. First of all i took a lead pencil and measured its weight, then i-put a small eraser on it and measured its weight.
Both the objects have less weight than the elastic limit of rubber band. That's why they could be measured easily.
I took a heavy stone and placed it in the balance.
But this mass was so heavy as compared to the elastic limit of the rubber band. Rubber band was broken and weight of the stone could not be measured.

## Unit 07:

## Properties of Matter

Q2. Write short answers to any FIVE (5) questions: $(5 \times 2=10)$
(i) Does there exist a fourth state of matter? What is that?
(FSD. GII, 2018) (DGK. GI, 2023)
(ii) What is meant by plasma? In this, gas occurs in which state?
(GRW. GII, BWP. GI, 2014) (FSD. GII, 2016) (BWP. GI, 2017) (MLN. GI, 2018) (SWL GII, 2019) (BWP. GI, 2023)

## $8.1+8.2$ Temperature and Heat + Thermometer

1. Water freezes at:
   (SGD. GI, 2017)
   (A) $0^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
   (B) $-32^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
   (C) 0 K
   (D) +273 K
   $\_\_\_\_$ of crocus is natural thermometer.
   (FSD. GI, 2016) (MLN, GI, 2017)
   (A) flower
   (B) seed
   (C) stem
   (D) root
2. Boiling point of gold is equal to:
   (GRW. Gl, 2018)
   (A) $2595^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (B) $2450^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (C) $2660^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (D) $1750^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
3. $50^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$ is equal to:
   (GRW. Gl, 2018) (FSD. Gl, 2022)
   (A) $110^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
   (B) $120^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
   (C) $122^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
   (D) $130^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
4. The thermometer is use to measure:
   (MLN. GII, 2019)
   (A) Temperature of body
   (B) Force
   (C) Length
   (D) Time
5. The boiling point of lead is:
   (RWP. GI, 2019)
   (A) $1750^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (B) $1751^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (C) $1752^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (D) $1753^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
6. The Crocus Flower opens at:
   (BWP. Gl, 2019)
   (A) $21^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (B) $22^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (C) $23^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (D) $24^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$

Answers

1. +273 K
2. flower
3. $2660^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
4. $122^{\circ} \mathrm{F}$
5. Temperature of body
6. $1750^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
7. $23^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$

### 8.3 Specific Heat Capacity

1. The specific heat of ice is:
   (MLN. GII, 2018)
   (A) $2100 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (B) $2200 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (C) $2300 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (D) $2400 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
2. The value of specific heat of dry soil is about:
   (MLN. GI, 2019)
   (A) $4200 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (B) $810 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (C) $700 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (D) $3000^{-} \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
3. The formula of specfic heat is:
   (RWP. Gl, 2019)
   (A) $\mathrm{c}=\frac{\Delta \mathrm{Q}}{\mathrm{m} \Delta \mathrm{t}}$
   (B) $c=\frac{m \Delta Q}{\Delta t}$
   (C) $\mathrm{c}=\frac{\Delta \mathrm{Q} \Delta \mathrm{t}}{\mathrm{m}}$
   (D) $\mathrm{c}=\frac{\Delta \mathrm{tm}}{\Delta \mathrm{Q}}$
4. Heat capacity of 5 kg of water having specific heat equal to $4200 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$ is:
   (RWP. GII, 2019)
   (A) $5 \mathrm{JK}^{-1}$
   (B) $21000 \mathrm{JK}^{-1}$
   (C) $840 \mathrm{JK}^{-1}$
   (D) $0.0011 \mathrm{JK}^{-1}$
5. The specific heat of sand is:
   (FSD. GII, 2021)
   (A) $835 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (B) $2100 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (C) $4200 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (D) $900 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
6. If " $\mathbf{m}$ " is the mass of a body and " $\mathbf{c}$ " is its specific heat, then its heat capacity is given by
   (SGD. GII, 2021)
   (A) $\frac{m}{c}$
   (B) $\frac{\mathrm{c}}{\mathrm{m}}$
   (C) mc
   (D) $\mathrm{mc}^{2}$

Answers 1. $2100 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$ 2. $810 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$ 3. $\mathrm{c}=\frac{\Delta \mathrm{Q}}{\mathrm{m} \Delta \mathrm{t}}$ 4. $21000 \mathrm{JK}^{-1}$ 5. $835 \mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$ 6. mc

## 8.5 + 8.8 Latent Heat of Fusion + Thermal Expansion

   (DGK GII, 2018)

   (B) $3.36 \times 10^{-5} \mathrm{~J} \mathrm{~kg}^{-1}$
   (C) $3.36 \times 10^{5} \mathrm{~J} \mathrm{~kg}^{-1}$
   (D) $2.26 \times 10^{5} \mathrm{~J} \mathrm{~kg}^{-1}$
   (A) $\Delta \mathrm{Q}=\mathrm{mH}_{\mathrm{f}}$
   (B) $\Delta Q=C H_{f}$
   (C) $\Delta Q=m C_{f} \Delta T$
   (D) $\Delta Q=m C_{f}$

   (LHR. GI, 2015) (FSD. GI, 2017) (LHR. GI, GRW. GII, DGK. GI, 2018) (SWL. GI, 2019) (DGK. GI, 2011) (FSD. GII, MLN. GI, 2022)

   (B) $\beta=3 \alpha$
   (C) $\beta=2 \alpha$
   (D) $\beta=\frac{\alpha}{2}$

   (B) $6 \times 10^{-5} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$

   (5WL. GII. 2014)

   (C) $1.9 \times 10^{-7} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$

   Answers
5. $3.36 \times 10^{5} \mathrm{~J} \mathrm{~kg}-12 . \Delta \mathrm{Q}=\mathrm{mH}_{\mathrm{f}}$

8. $1.9 \times 10^{-5} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$

or $\quad \mathrm{C}=27^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$ 4. Define centripetal force and centrifugal force.
(LHR. GI, 2014) (RWP. GI, 2016) (SWL. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, 2023)
Ans. Centripetal force: Centripetal force is a force that keeps a body to move in a circle.
Centrifugal force: Consider a stone tied to a string moving in a circle. The necessary centripetal force acts on the stone through the string that keeps it to move in a circle. According to Newton's third law of motion, there exists a reaction to this centripetal force. Centripetal reaction that pulls the string outward is sometimes called the centrifugal force. 5. Define specific heat capacity and write its formula and SI unit. (LHR. GI, 2018) (FSD. GII, BWP. GII, 2019)
(SWL GII, BWP. GI, 2021) (LHR. GI, FSD. GI \& GII, BWP. GI, 2023)
Ans. The specific heat of a substance is the amount of heat required to raise the temperature of 1 kg mass of that substance through 1 K .
Specific heat of any substance can be found out by using following formula:

$$
c=\frac{\Delta Q}{m \Delta T}
$$

Unit: The SI unit of specific heat is $\mathrm{Jkg}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$. 6. What is meant by Evaporation?
(SGD. GI, 2019) (DGK. GII, BWP. GII, RWP. GII, 2021) (FSD. GI, 2022) (BWP. GII, 2023)
Ans. Evaporation: Evaporation is the changing of a liquid into vapours (gaseous state) from the surface of the liquid without heating it. 7. What is difference between linear thermal expansion and volume thermal expansion.

Ans.
(FSD. GII, 2018)

| Linear thermal expansion                                                                                                                                                   | Volume thermal expansion                                                                             |
| :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | :--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| The expansion in a solid upon heating is called linear thermal expansion. Solids expand on heating and their expansion is nearly uniform over a wide range of temperature. | The volume of a solid changes with the change in temperature and is called volume thermal expansion. |

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

5.2: Why does heat flow from hot body to cold body?
(MLN. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2014) (DGK. GII, 2015) (FSD. GII, 2016) (FSD. GII, 2018) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, BWP. GI, 2022)
Ans. Heat flows from hot body to cold body to attain the condition of thermal equilibrium.
0.3: Define the terms heat and temperature.
(FSD. GII, SWL GI, LHR. GI, GRW. GI, DGK. GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (FSD. GI \& GI, MLN. GI \& GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, SGD. GI \& GI, 2021)
(LHR. GI \& GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, MLN. GI, SWL GI, 2022) (GRW. GI \& GI, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, 2023)
Ans. Heat: Heat is the energy that is transferred from one body to the other in thermal contact with each other as a result of the difference of temperature between them.
Temperature: Temperature of a body is the degree of hotness or coldness of the body.
0.7: What is meant by internal energy of a body?
(GRW. GI \& GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GI, 2018) (SWL. GII, SGD. GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI \& GI, 2019) (LHR. GI \& GI, BWP. GI, SGD. GI, 2021)
(GRW. GI, FSD. GII, MLN. GII, SGD. GII, RWP. GII, 2022) (LHR. GI, MLN GII, SWL GI, SGD. GI \& GII, 2023)
Ans. The sum of kinetic energy and potential energy associated with the atoms, molecules and particles of a body is called its internal energy.
How does heating affect the motion of molecules of a gas?
(LHR. GII, 2015) (LHR. GII, 2018) (MLN. GI, RWP. GI, 2019) (BWP. GII, 2014) (SGD. GII, 2022)
Ans. By heating the gas, its molecules get high kinetic energy and start to collide more randomly. And motion of gas molecules is increased by heating. So pressure of gas molecules increase by heating.
3.0. What is a thermometer? Why mercury is preferred as a thermometric substance?
(SWL. GII, 2014) (GRW. GII, DGK. GI, 2015)(SGD. GII, 2017)(MLN. GII, 2018) (DGK. GII, BWR. GII, 2022)
Ans. A thermometer is a device which is used to measure the temperature of a body.
Mercury is preferred as a thermometric substance due to following properties.
It is easily visible.
It has low freezing point and high boiling point.

- It has uniform thermal expansion.

It has a small specific heat capacity.
8.7: Explain the volumetric thermal expansion. (Subjective Type Question)
(MLN. GI, 2019)
Ans. For answer see "Hámdard Imtihani Physics "9".
N.8. Define specific heat. How would you find the specific heat of a solid?

Ans. The specific heat of a substance is the amount of heat required to raise the temperature of 1 kg mass of that substance through 1 K .
Specific heat of any substance can be found out by using following formula:
$c=\frac{\Delta Q}{m \Delta T}$
c is the specific heat capacity
$\Delta \mathrm{Q}$ is the amount of heat absorbed by the body
m is the mass of the body.
$\Delta \mathrm{T}$ is the change of temperature
8.19 Define and explain latent heat of fusion. (Subjective Type Question)
(LHR. GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, RWP. GI, 2018) (LHR. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, GRW. GI, 2021) (LHR. GI, DGK. GI, 2022)
Ans. For answer see "Hamdard Imtihani Physics "9".
S.I (1): Define latent heat of vaporization.(FSD. GI, BWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GII, FSD.GI,MLM.GI,2021) (SGD.GI.RWP.GI.2022) (MLM.GII, 2013]

Ans. The quantity of heat that changes unit mass of a liquid completely into gas at its boiling point without any change in its temperature is called its latent heat of vaporization denoted by $\mathrm{H}_{\mathrm{v}}$.

$$
\mathrm{H}_{\mathrm{v}}=\frac{\Delta \mathrm{Qv}}{\mathrm{~m}}
$$

S.11: What is meant by evaporation? On what factors the evaporation of a liquid depends? Explain how cooling is produced by evaporation. (LHR. GI. SGD. GI, DGK. GI, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, 2016)(RWP. GI, 2017)
Ans. Evaporation: Evaporation is the changing of a liquid into vapours (gaseous state) from the surface of the liquid without heating it.
Factors which affect on evaporation; The rate of evaporation is affected by the following factors.
(i) Temperature
(ii) Surface area
(iii) Wind
(iv) Nature of the liquid

Evaporation causes cooling: As evaporation takes place, fast moving molecules escape out from the surface of the liquid. Molecules that have lower kinetic energies are left behind.

This lowers the average kinetic energy of the liquids molecules and the temperature of the liquid. Since temperature of a substance depends on the average kinetic energy of its molecules, therefore the temperature of the liquid decreases.

NOTE:Four possible answers A, B, C and D to each question are given. The choice which you think is correct, fill that circle in front of that question with Marker or Pen ink. Cutting or filling two or more circles will result in zero mark in that question. 01.

1. Mercury freezes at:
   (A) $0^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (B) $-357^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (C) $-39^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$

   (BWP. Gl, 2014) (BWP. Gl, 2023)

   (B) low freezing point
   (C) small heat capacity

   (B) $78^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$
   (C) $100^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$

   (B) 373 K
   (C) $-273^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$

   (A) 273 K
   (B) 293 K
   (C) 300 K
   (D) 373 K

   (B) $\mathrm{H}_{\mathrm{m}}$

    (B) Surface area of the liquid

    (GRW. Gl, FSD. Gl, 2021)

    (B) $\mathrm{L}_{\mathrm{O}}(1-\alpha \Delta \mathrm{T})$
    (C) $\mathrm{L}_{\mathrm{o}}(\alpha \Delta \mathrm{T})$
    (D) $\mathrm{L}_{\mathrm{O}}(1+\alpha \Delta \mathrm{T})$

    (A) $\beta=\frac{\Delta T}{V_{0} \Delta V}$
    (B) $\beta=\frac{\Delta V}{\Delta T}$

## $9.2+9.3$ Conduction + Convection

1. Ways to transfer of heat are:
   (MLN. GII, 2016) (MLN. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, SWL. GI \& GII, BWP. GI, SGD. GI, 2021)
   (A) 1
   (B) 2
   (C) 3
   (D) 4
2. Thermal conductivity of water is:
   (SWL GI, RWP. GII, 2017)
   (A) $0.59 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (B) $0.8 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (C) $0.6 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (D) $1.7 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
3. Thermal conductivity of Ice is:
   (BWP. GII, 2017)
   (A) $1.8 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (B) $1.9 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (C) $1.7 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
   (D) $2.0 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$
4. Rate of flow of heat through conductor is inversely proportional to its:
   (FSD. GII, 2018)
   (A) Area
   (B) Length
   (C) Temperature
   (D) Time
5. For quick heat transfer sauce pan are made of:
   (FSD. Gl, 2019)
   (A) Wood
   (B) Metal
   (C) Plastic
   (D) Fiber glass
6. Convection of heat is the process of heat of molecules transferred due to:
   (FSD. GII, 2017)
   (A) linear motion of molecules
   (B) downward movement of molecules
   (C) upward movement of molecules
   (D) free movement of molecules

Answers 1.32.0.59 $\mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1} 3.1 .7 \mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1} 4$. Length 5. Metal 6. upward movement of molecules
