## Short Questions developed according to the New Examination Techniques (Knowledge, Understanding, Application, Analytical and Conceptual) of the Education Department.

## 9.1+9.2 Transfer of Heal + Conduction

1.

What is transfer of heat? Write the names of its method.
(FSD. GII, DGK GH, 2017) (MLN. GI, RWP. GII, 2018)
(SGD. GII, 2019) (GRW. GI, SWL. GI \& GI, SGD. GH, 2021) (FSD. GI, 2022) (LHR. GI, FSD. GI, SGD. GII, 202]
Ans. Transfer of heat: When two bodies at different temperature are in thermal contact with each other. Thermal energy from a hot body flows to the cold body in the form of heat.
This is called as transfer of the heat.
Ways of heat transfer: There are three ways by which transfer of heat takes place.
(i) Conduction
(ii) Convection
(iii) Radiation 2. What is meant by conduction? (GRW. GI, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, 2018) (LHR. GII, 2019) (MLN. GII, 2021) (MLN. GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GI.2023)

Ans. Conduction: The mode of transfer of heat by vibrating atoms and free electrons in solids from hot to cold parts of a body is called conduction of heat. 3. Define thermal conductivity and write its SI unit.
(DGK. GI, BWP. Gi, 2018)
(LHR. GI, GRW. GII, MLN, GII, SWL GI, SGD. GI \& GI, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2019)(LHR GII, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, DGK. GI, 2021) (MLN. GI, 2022)
Ans. The rate of flow of heat across the opposite faces of a metre cube of a substance maintained at a temperature difference of one kelvin.
Unit: The SI unit of thermal conductivity is $\mathrm{Wm}^{-1} \mathrm{~K}^{-1}$. 4. Describe the rate of flow of heat. What is its mathematical form?
(MLN. GH, DGK. GI, BWP. GI, 2021) (SWL. GI, DGK. GII, 2023)
Ans. The amount of heat flows in unit time is called the rate of flow of heat.
Rate of flow of heat: $\frac{Q}{t}=\frac{K A\left(T_{1}-T_{2}\right)}{L}$ 5. How does cross sectional area of solid affect thermal conductivity?
(LHR GI, 2017)
Ans. Larger cross-sectional area A of a solid contains larger numbers of molecules and free electrons on each layer parallel to its cross-sectional area and hence greater will be the rate of flow of heat through solid. Thus:

Rate of flow of heat: $\frac{\mathrm{Q}}{\mathrm{t}} \propto \mathrm{A}$ 6. How many factors affect thermal conductivity? Also write their names. (DGK GI, 2017)(DGK. GI, 2019)

Ans. 1. Cross-sectional area of the solid (A) 2. Length of the solid (L). 3. Temperature difference between the hot and cold ends $\left(T_{1}-T_{2}\right)$ 4.Nature of the material of the solid 7. Write the uses of Conductors and Non-conductors.

Ans. Uses of conductors:
(FSD. GII, SWL GII, 2018) (MLN. GL, 2019)

1. Good conductors are used when quick transfer of heat is required through a body. Thus cookers, cooking plates, boilers, radiators and condensers of refrigerators, etc. are made up of metals such as aluminium and copper for the better conduction.
2. Metal boxes are used for making ice, ice cream etc.

Uses of non-conductors:

1. Insulators or bad conductors are used in home utensils such as handles of sauce-pans, hot plates, spoons etc. They are made up of wood or plastic.
2. Air is one of the bad conductors or best insulator.

That is why cavity walls i.e two walls separated by an air space and double glazed windows keep the houses warm in winter and cool in summer.

## 9.3 + 9.4 Convection + Radiation

1. What is meant by convection?
   (LHR. GII, 2019) (FSD. GII, 2021) (LHR. GI, FSD. GII, BWP, GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Transfer of heat by actual movement of molecules from hot place to a cold place is known as convection.
   Exmaple: Balloons inflated with hot air rise up.
2. Describe use of convection currents. (SGD. GI, 2017)(LHR. GII, GRW. GI, MLN. GI, SWL GI, BWP. GI, 2018) (SWL. GI, 2019)
   (LHR GII, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, SWL GI, DGK, CII, 2021) (SCD. GII, RWP. GI, 2022) (MLN. GH, BWP. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Uses of convection currents: Convection currents occur on a large scale in nature. Some uses of convection currents are as;

- Convection currents set up by electric, gas or coal heaters help to warm our homes and offices.
- Central heating systems in buildings work on the same principle by convection.
- The day-to-day temperature changes in the atmosphere result from the circulation of warm or cold air that travels across the region.
- Land and sea breezes are also the examples of convection current.

3. What causes a glider to remain in air? (SGD, GI, 2014) (RWP. GI, SWL, GI, DGK, GI, 2015) (MLN. GII, 2016) (LHR. GII, DGK. GII, 2017) (RWP. GII, 2018) (DGK. GII, 2019) (FSD. GI, MLN. GI, SGD. GI, DGK GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, FSD. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Gliders ride over these thermals. The upward movement of air currents in thermals help gliders to stay in air for a long period.
4. Differentiate between land breeze and sea breeze.
   (LHR. GII, DGK. GII, 2014)
   (GRW. GI, MLN. GI, SWL. GI, RWP. GII, 2016) (GRW. GI, MLN. GII, 2017) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI,FSD. GI, MLN. GI, SGD. GI \& GI, RWP. GI, 2018)
   (LHR. GI, GRW. GI, FSD. GI, SWL GI, 2019) (FSD. GII, BWP. GI, SGD. GI, 2021) (MLN. GI \& GII, DGK. GI, 2022) (GRW. GI, FSD. GI, MLN. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Sea breeze: On a hot day, the temperature of the land increases more quickly than the sea. It is because the specific heat of land is much smaller as compared to water. The air above land gets hot and rise up. The cold air from the sea begins to move towards the land. It is called sea breeze.
   Land breeze: At night, the land cools faster than the sea. Therefore, air above the sea is warmer, rises up and the colder air from the land begins to move towards the sea as shown in given figure. It is called land breeze.
5. Differentiate between conduction and convection. (FSD.GI,2015)(SGD.GII,2017)(MLN. GI, 2018)(MLN. GII, SWL. GI, 2019)
   (GRW. GII, SGD. GII, RWP. GI, DGK. GI, 2021) (GRW. GI, SGD. GI, DGK. GII, 2022) (FSD. GII, RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2023)
   Ans. Conduction: The mode of transfer of heat by vibrating atoms and free electrons in solids from hot to cold parts of a body is called conduction of heat.
   Convection: Transfer of heat by actual movement of molecules from hot place to a cold place is known as convection.
6. Write names of any two birds who are expert thermal climbers? (RWP. GI, BWP. GI, 2017) (LHR. GI, 2018)

Ans. Eagles, hawks and vultures. 7. How do Thermals help birds to fly for hours without flapping their wings?
(BWP. G., 2019)
Ans. The birds stretch out their wings and circle in thermals. The upwards movement of air helps birds to climb up with it. 8. What is meant by radiation?
(MLN. GI, 2014) (DGK. GI \& GII, BWP. GII, 2016) (GRW. GI \& GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GI, 2017)
(LHR. GI \& GII, RWP. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GII, 2018) (LHR. GII, 2019) (MLN. GI, DGK. GII, BWP. GII, 2022) (SWL. GII, RWP. GII, 2023)
Ans. Radiation is the mode of transfer of heat from one place to another in the form of waves called electromagnetic waves. 9. How does heat reach us from the Sun?
(DGK. GI, 2018) (RWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, FSD. GI, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2021)
(SWL GI, RWP. GI, 2022) (MLN. GII, SWL GI, RWP. GI, BWP. GL, 2023)
Ans. Heat reaches us from the Sun through radiation process. 10. What is Leslie cube? Write the names of its surfaces.
(DGK GL, 2017)
Ans. A Leslie cube is a metal box having faces of different nature. Various surfaces can be compared using Leslie cube.
Leslie cube has four surfaces:

1. A shining silvered surface 2. A dull black surface 3. A white surface 4. A coloured surface
2. Mention the use of Leslie's cube.
   (FSD. GII, 2016) (RWP. GII, 2019)
   Ans. A Leslie cube is a metal box having faces of different nature. The rate at which various surfaces emit
   heat depends upon the nature of the surface, various surfaces can be compared using Leslie cube.

## Exercise (Short Answer Questions)

0.2. Why are metals good conductors of heat?
(MLN. GI, SGD. GI, 2017)(MLN. GII, RWP. GII, DGK. GII, 2019) (SGD. GII, 2021)
(FSD. GI, SGD. GI, 2022) (SGD. GI, DGK. GI, 2023)
Ans. Metals are good conductors of heat because metal contains free electrons which can move from one place to another, by getting energy.
At the hot end, they get energy from the hot flame and move towards cold end, transferring energy to the other atoms and electron by collision on their way. At the same time atoms at the hot end, start vibrating more vigorously and transfer some energy by collision to neighbouring atoms, eventually heating the other end.
0.3. Explain why:
(a) A metal feels colder to touch than wood kept in a cold place?
(b) Land breeze blows from land towards sea?
(DGK. Gl, 2014)(FSD. Gl, 2017)
(c) Double walled glass vessel is used in thermos flask?
(RWP. Gl, 2019)
(d) Deserts soon get hot during the day and soon get cold after sunset?

Ans. (a) A metal feels colder to touch than wood because it is a good conductor due to free electrons. So it cools down more rapidly as compared to wood. Wood is an example of insulator
(b) At night, the land cools faster than the sea.

Therefore, air above the sea is warmer, rises up and colder air from the land begins to move towards the sea.
(c) Double walled glass vessel is used in thermosflask because double walled glass vessel has air between two glass walls that provide insulation.
(d) Deserts soon get hot during the day and soon get cold after sunset because sand in the deserts has very low value of specific heat.
It cools down and warms up fastly.
9.7: Why conduction of heat does not take place in gases?
(FSD. GI, RWP, GII, 2021) (LHR. GI \& GII, SWL GII, 2027)
Ans. Conduction is the process of transfer of heat by vibrating atoms and free electrons in solids from hotter to colder parts of the body while convection is the process of transfer of heat by actual movement of molecules from hot place to cold place. So in the gases, molecules do not vibrate at their places, due to weak intermolecular forces, the molecules actually move from their places. Thats way the conduction of heat does not take place in gases.

## 9.5: What measures do you suggest to conserve energy in houses? (LHR GI\& GI, RWP. G. 2016) (DGK. GI, 2019)

Ans. Energy in houses can be conserved by using energy savers instead of bulbs.

- Switch off the electric appliances when these are not used by humans.
- Geothermal energy can be used to heat up, water into steam for the utilization of cooking food.
- Solar energy is used by solar panel in houses.

The solar energy is converted into electric energy.

- The bottoms of cooking pots are made black to increase the absorption of heat from fire.
- Hot water tanks are insulated by plastic or foam lagging.
- Wall cavities are filled with plastic foam or wool.
- False ceiling is done using insulating materials.
- Double glazed window panes are used. These window panes have air between glass sheets that provides insulation.
  2.6: Why does transfer of heat in fluids take place by convection? (SWL GII, RWP. GI, 2027) (MLN. GII, 2022)

Ans. Convection is a process of transfer of heat by actual movement of molecules from hot place to a cold place. As we know the intermolecular forces are less in fluids as compared to solid, due to weak intermolecular forces the fluids molecules can move from their actual positions and are responsible for the transfer of heat by convection process.

## 9.7: What is meant by convection current?

(LHR. GI, 2018) (FSD. GII, BWP. GII, 2019) (GRW. GII, SWL GII, BWP. GII, SGD. GI, 2021) (FSD. GI, MLN. GI, 2023)
Ans. The path flow or current which is used for the transfer of heat by actual movement of molecules for hot place to a cold place is known as convection current.
9.8: Suggest a simple activity to show convection of heat in gases not given in the book.

Ans. An example of convection in daily life is when we use a fire place to heat our home, as the fire heats up the air in front of it, the hot air rises up as it is less dense and than in turn pushes the cool air down so that it is heated and then rises, this motion is called convection currents and is the reason why fire place air effective to heat us.
9.9: How does heat reach us from the Sun? (DGK. GI, 2015) (LHR. GII, FSD. GII, SGD. GI, 2016) (FSD. GI, 2017)
(DGK. GI, 2018) (RWP. GI, 2019) (LHR. GI, FSD. GI, MLN. GI \& GII, SGD. GI, RWP. GI, 2021) (SWL GI, RWP. GI, 2022)
Ans. Heat reaches us from the Sun through radiation process.
9.10: How various surfaces can be compared by a Leslie cube?

Ans. A Lesile cube is a metal box having faces of different nature.

- A shining silvered surface
- A white surface

A dull black surface
A coloured surface

Black dull surface is a good emitter of heat.
A dull black surface is a good absorber of heat as its temperature rises rapidly:
A polished surface is poor absorber of heat as its temperature rises very slowly.
Larger is the area, greater will be the transfer of heat.
9.11: What is greenhouse effect?
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/5f3e6344-6e74-4eaa-a082-47486227f9cc-68.jpg?height=378&width=192&top_left_y=1536&top_left_x=1241)
(GRW. GII, FSD. GI, SWL GI \& GII, SGD. GI, BWP. GII, 2019) (LHR. GII, GRW. GI, FSD, GII, SGD. GII, 2022) (MLN. GII, SWL. GII, DGK GII, 203] Ans. In the environment, carbondioxide and water also behave in a similar way to radiations as glass or polythene. Glass and transparent polythene sheets allow radiations of short wavelengths to pass through easily but not long wavelengths of thermal radiations. Thus, a green-house becomes a heat trap. Radiations from the Sun pass easily through glass and warms up the objects in a greenhouse. The objects and plants in greenhouse give out radiation of much longer wavelengths and do no allow them to escape out easily and are reflected back in the greenhouse. Similarly Earth's atmosphere contains carbondioxide and water vapours. It causes greenhouse effect and thus maintains the temperature of the earth.
9.12: Explain the impact of greenhouse effect in global warming.
(MLN. GII, SWP, GII, 2014) (BWP. GI, 2019)
Ans. During the recent years, the percentage of carbon dioxide has been increased considerably. This has caused an increase in the average temperature of the Earth by trapping more heat due to greenhouse effect. This phenomenon is known as global warming. This has serious implications for global climate.
